Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
app.frontend() with fallback="index.html" returns 404 for client side routes that have a dot in the last path segment (like /users/john.doe or /v/1.2.3)

### Discussed in https://github.com/fastapi/fastapi/discussions/15979

<div type='discussions-op-text'>

<sup>Originally posted by **UditDewan** July 12, 2026</sup>
### First Check

### Commit to Help

- [x] I commit to help with one of those options 👆

### Example Code

```python
import os
import tempfile

from fastapi import FastAPI
from fastapi.testclient import TestClient

dist = tempfile.mkdtemp()
with open(os.path.join(dist, "index.html"), "w") as f:
    f.write("<html>SPA shell</html>")

app = FastAPI()
app.frontend("/", directory=dist, fallback="index.html")

client = TestClient(app)

# The Accept header a browser sends on a normal top level navigation.
browser_nav = {
    "accept": "text/html,application/xhtml+xml,application/xml;q=0.9,"
    "image/avif,image/webp,image/apng,*/*;q=0.8"
}

print(client.get("/users/john", headers=browser_nav).status_code)      # 200, serves index.html
print(client.get("/users/john.doe", headers=browser_nav).status_code)  # 404
print(client.get("/v/1.2.3", headers=browser_nav).status_code)         # 404
```

### Description

Hi 👋

I have been trying out the new `app.frontend()` helper to serve a single page app, using `fallback="index.html"` so that client side routes fall back to the shell and the frontend router can take over. This is the behavior described in the "Client side routing" part of the docs, and it works fine for a path like `/dashboard` or `/dashboard/settings`.

The problem shows up when a client side route has a dot in its last path segment. Plenty of real apps have these, for example a profile at `/users/john.doe`, a version deep link at `/v/1.2.3`, or a slug like `/files/report.2024`. When I open one of those directly, or just hit refresh while I am already on that page, I get a 404 instead of the `index.html` shell, so the app never loads and the client router never gets a chance to handle the route.

The part that surprised me is that setting `fallback="index.html"` explicitly does not change this. As far as I can tell there is currently no way to get these routes to fall back to the shell.

I spent some time reading the code and I think it comes from `_is_frontend_navigation_request()` in `fastapi/routing.py`. It takes the last path segment and if `os.path.splitext(...)` finds an extension it returns early and treats the request as an asset request, before it ever looks at the `Accept` header. Because `os.path.splitext("john.doe")` returns `.doe`, any segment with a dot in it is treated as a file and never gets the `index.html` fallback, even when the browser clearly asked for `text/html`.

What makes me think this is fixable without regressions is that the two situations are easy to tell apart. A real browser navigation sends `Accept: text/html`, while a missing asset requested from a script tag, an image tag, or a fetch call sends `*/*` or a specific type like `text/css`. If I request a genuinely missing asset such as `/assets/missing.js` with `Accept: */*` it still returns 404 as expected, so checking the `Accept` header first would fix the navigation case and keep the asset case working.

I did notice there is already a test that pins the current behavior. `test_index_fallback_does_not_handle_asset_like_or_non_html_requests` has a `("/users/jane.doe", "text/html")` case that expects a 404, so before proposing a change I wanted to ask whether the current behavior is intentional. If the idea is that dotted client routes should be servable, would a change that treats an explicit `Accept: text/html` request as navigation regardless of the path be acceptable? Or would you rather keep the extension heuristic as the default for `fallback="auto"` and add an opt in for apps that use dotted client side routes?

I am happy to open a PR with a failing test and the change for whichever direction you prefer. Thanks a lot for the work on this feature.

### Operating System

Windows

### Operating System Details

Also reproduced on current master. The logic involved is pure routing code, so it is not tied to any particular operating system.

### FastAPI Version

0.139.0

### Pydantic Version

2.13.4

### Python Version

3.11

### Additional Context

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
Race condition in _IncludedRouter cache rebuild can 404 valid routes and permanently corrupt the candidate cache
### Description

Since the router refactor in 0.137.0 (#15745), `_IncludedRouter.effective_candidates()` and `_IncludedRouter.effective_low_priority_routes()` in `fastapi/routing.py` rebuild their cached lists lazily on first use, with no synchronization.

The rebuild publishes an empty list on the shared attribute first, appends routes into it one by one, and only stamps the version at the end:

```python
self._effective_candidates = []
# ... appends into self._effective_candidates in a loop ...
self._effective_candidates_version = routes_version
```

If several threads drive the app's first requests at the same time (for example per-thread `TestClient`s in a parallel test suite, or any embedding that serves one app object from multiple event loops), more than one thread can pass the version check and rebuild concurrently. Every rebuilder appends into whichever list was assigned to the attribute last, so the cache ends up with duplicated candidates, and the corruption is permanent because the version gets stamped anyway. A request that runs while the list is still partially built can also get a 404 for a route that exists.

The rebuild path additionally uses `warnings.catch_warnings()` internally (via response field construction), so interleaved rebuilds can leak entries into the global warnings filters.

### Reproduction

```python
import sys
import threading

from fastapi import APIRouter, FastAPI
from fastapi.routing import _IncludedRouter
from fastapi.testclient import TestClient

N_ROUTES = 120
N_THREADS = 6

app = FastAPI()
router = APIRouter()
for i in range(N_ROUTES):
    def endpoint(i: int = i):
        return {"i": i}
    router.add_api_route(f"/r{i}", endpoint, methods=["GET"])
app.include_router(router)

sys.setswitchinterval(1e-5)  # widen the rebuild window
barrier = threading.Barrier(N_THREADS)

def worker():
    client = TestClient(app)
    barrier.wait()
    client.get(f"/r{N_ROUTES - 1}")

threads = [threading.Thread(target=worker) for _ in range(N_THREADS)]
for t in threads:
    t.start()
for t in threads:
    t.join()

included = next(r for r in app.router.routes if isinstance(r, _IncludedRouter))
print(len(included._effective_candidates), "cached candidates, expected", N_ROUTES)
```

On my machine this reliably prints around 600 cached candidates for the 120 route app.

### Expected behavior

The cache rebuild should be thread safe. Building the list into a local variable and publishing it atomically (list first, version second) keeps readers from ever seeing a partial list, and serializing the rebuild avoids the duplicated appends and the warnings filter leak.

### Environment

- FastAPI version: 0.139.0
- Python version: 3.14.5
- OS: Windows 11

Related report: discussion #15914 describes the same symptoms.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
`_is_hf_initialized` per-param check doesn't skip redundant init for built-in models on non-CUDA hardware
### System Info

- `transformers` version: 4.57.6
- Platform: Ascend NPU 910B, CANN 8.5.0
- Python version: 3.11
- PyTorch version: 2.9.0, torch_npu 2.9.0
- Hardware: 16 × Ascend 910B, FSDP2

### Who can help?

_No response_

### Information

- [ ] The official example scripts
- [x] My own modified scripts

### Tasks

- [ ] An officially supported task in the `examples` folder (such as GLUE/SQuAD, ...)
- [x] My own task or dataset (give details below)

### Reproduction

```python
# Minimal reproduction: any built-in model under FSDP on Ascend NPU
# The _is_hf_initialized per-param flags are completely ignored for non-custom-code models

from transformers import AutoModel
import torch
import torch.distributed as dist
import torch_npu

# 1. Init FSDP process group
dist.init_process_group(backend='hccl')

# 2. Load a built-in model (NOT trust_remote_code)
model = AutoModel.from_pretrained("google/umt5-small")

# 3. Under FSDP2, _initialize_missing_keys() sets _is_hf_initialized = True
#    on all params of non-rank0 processes.
#    But _initialize_weights() NEVER reads those flags because is_custom_code=False.

# 4. Result: all non-rank0 ranks call _init_weights() → normal_() on every param.
#    On Ascend NPU, normal_ is ~1000x slower than CUDA (~1s vs ~1ms per large tensor).
#    For a large model: 219 redundant normal_ calls × 16 ranks = ~224s wasted.

# Root cause location: modeling_utils.py L2564-2574
# _check_per_param_flag = is_custom_code  ← built-in models always False here
```


### Expected behavior

### Root Cause

`_initialize_weights()` in `modeling_utils.py` has a per-parameter `_is_hf_initialized` check at L2564-2574. The variable `_check_per_param_flag` is set to `is_custom_code`, which is `False` for all built-in models (UMT5, BERT, T5, etc.). This makes the per-param flag check dead code for those models — even though `_initialize_missing_keys()` at L4882 correctly sets the flags on all params of non-rank0 FSDP processes.

### Why it matters on Ascend NPU

`torch.nn.init.normal_` on Ascend NPU is ~1000x slower than CUDA (~1s vs ~1ms per large tensor). Each call triggers a full kernel compilation and launch. Under FSDP2, every non-rank0 process redundantly initializes all params via `_init_weights()` → `normal_()`, even though those params will be overwritten by rank0's broadcast.

### Measured Impact (MOVA training, 16 × Ascend 910B)

| Metric | Before fix | After fix | Delta |
|--------|-----------|-----------|-------|
| Training launch | 463s | 136s | **−71%** |
| Redundant `normal_` calls skipped | — | 219 per rank | — |

### Precision Validation

Verified that skipping redundant `_init_weights` on already-initialized params has zero precision impact:

- 16 ranks × 4397 parameters: weight fingerprints **all bit-level identical**
- 2-step loss: MAE=0.000e+00 across all 16 ranks for loss / v_loss / a_loss

### Proposed Fix

Minimal, NPU-scoped (PR #47335 v3):

```python
# modeling_utils.py L2566
_check_per_param_flag = is_custom_code
if not _check_per_param_flag:
    try:
        import torch_npu
        _check_per_param_flag = True
    except ImportError:
        pass
```

`is_torch_npu_available()` → `False` when `torch_npu` not installed — zero impact on CUDA/ROCm/XPU.

Or more generally, just remove the `is_custom_code` gate. The per-param flag is only set by `_initialize_missing_keys` (FSDP path), so skipping `_init_weights` for flagged params should be safe for all model types.

### Related

- PR #47335: fix with `is_torch_npu_available()` gate (v3), reviewed by @Rocketknight1
- Ascend NPU maintainer: @ivarflakstad

cc @Rocketknight1 @ivarflakstad
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
Several slow tokenizers read all_special_tokens or all_special_ids once per token in decode loops
### Who can help?

@itazap

### Summary

Same pattern as #46315 and #46396, third instance. `all_special_tokens` and `all_special_ids` are properties that rebuild their list on every access (`all_special_ids` additionally calls `convert_tokens_to_ids` on each special token). The base class knows this and hoists the lookup before its loop in `tokenization_python.py` (the comment there says "may be slow, so only compute it once before the loop"), but several model tokenizers still read the property once per token inside their decode or mask loops:

- `esm`: `get_special_tokens_mask` list comprehension reads `self.all_special_ids` per id
- `marian`, `m2m_100`, `speech_to_text`, `gpt_sw3`, `siglip`: `convert_tokens_to_string` reads `self.all_special_tokens` per token

Measured on ESM with 20k ids: `get_special_tokens_mask(..., already_has_special_tokens=True)` takes 26.8 ms on main and 0.3 ms with the lookup hoisted to a set before the loop, identical output. Protein sequences and ASR outputs are exactly the inputs where these token counts are routine.

Two related observations while auditing, left out of the fix on purpose:

- `wav2vec2` has the same pattern in `convert_ids_to_tokens`, but #46578 (open) touches that exact line, so I left it to avoid conflicting with that PR.
- `wav2vec2_phoneme` (`_decode`, line ~427) checks `token in self.all_special_ids`, comparing a token string against a list of ints. That branch can never be true as written; convert_ids_to_tokens above it already handles the skip, so it looks like dead code rather than a live bug, but flagging it since you may want to clean it up or make it check `all_special_tokens` instead.

PR with the six hoists incoming, linked to this issue.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
CompressedTensorsConfig(run_compressed=False) silently random-initializes unmapped fused-MoE expert weights on 5.10.x (works on 5.13.1) — request hard error for unmapped packed tensors
**Summary**: Loading a compressed-tensors W4A16 checkpoint of `Qwen/Qwen3.6-35B-A3B` (fused-expert MoE) with `from_pretrained(ckpt, quantization_config=CompressedTensorsConfig(run_compressed=False))` on **transformers 5.10.1** prints:

```
model.language_model.layers.{0...39}.mlp.experts.gate_up_proj_packed | UNEXPECTED
model.language_model.layers.{0...39}.mlp.experts.gate_up_proj        | MISSING
model.language_model.layers.{0...39}.mlp.experts.down_proj           | MISSING
```

i.e. the decompressor does not map the packed fused expert tensors, and those weights are **silently newly-initialized** — the returned "trainable QDQ model" produces garbage logits for every MoE layer while `from_pretrained` "succeeds". This breaks QAT/recovery-training workflows. (Diagnostic: the broken student's logits agree 97% with an independently-loaded copy of itself, but 0% with the uncorrupted teacher.)

**Environment (broken)**: transformers 5.10.1, compressed-tensors 0.17.1.

**Resolution verified**: on transformers **5.13.1** the same flow decompresses correctly (per-expert checkpoint tensors are mapped into the fused module via the conversion-mapping loader; we verified the QDQ values match a manual dequant of the packed weights to 2.4e-4 max abs error).

**Request**: on versions/paths where packed tensors cannot be mapped, please **raise a hard error instead of silently newly-initializing weights**. Silent random init behind a successful `from_pretrained` is the worst failure mode for downstream training pipelines.
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
Silent conversion skip on model_type mismatch: loading a converted checkpoint via the wrong Auto class yields randomly-initialized weights that generate fluently
### System Info

- `transformers` version: 5.14.1
- Platform: Linux-6.17.0-1007-aws-x86_64-with-glibc2.39
- Python version: 3.12.3
- Huggingface_hub version: 1.24.0
- Safetensors version: 0.8.0
- Accelerate version: 1.14.0
- Accelerate config: not found
- DeepSpeed version: not installed
- PyTorch version (accelerator?): 2.12.0a0+git220ecc2 (CUDA)
- Using distributed or parallel set-up in script?: No (single process; reproduces with device_map="auto" or single GPU)
- Using GPU in script?: Yes
- GPU type: NVIDIA B300 SXM6 AC
Supplementary: transformers 5.14.1; torch 2.12.0a0 cu12.9; model: Inkling-975B (multimodal, `model_type: inkling_mm_model`, converted checkpoint).


### Who can help?

@CyrilVallez (model loading / conversion mapping) @zucchini-nlp (multimodal)
 


### Information

- [ ] The official example scripts
- [x] My own modified scripts

### Tasks

- [ ] An officially supported task in the `examples` folder (such as GLUE/SQuAD, ...)
- [x] My own task or dataset (give details below)

### Reproduction

Checkpoint conversion mappings are resolved by the **loaded class's** expectations; when a user loads a converted checkpoint through a class whose naming doesn't match (e.g. `AutoModelForCausalLM` on a checkpoint whose weights live under the multimodal layout), no conversion table applies and every checkpoint tensor fails to match:
 
```python
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM
m = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(PATH_TO_INKLING, dtype="bfloat16")  # multimodal ckpt
out = m.generate(**tok("The capital of France is", return_tensors="pt"), max_new_tokens=8)
# -> fluent but random text ("empatan ..."); no error raised
```
Symptoms in the log: "load" completes in seconds for a 1.9 TB checkpoint; conversion progress shows `0it`; the only signals are symmetric MISSING/UNEXPECTED key warnings (easily lost in noise) — then the model **generates fluent garbage** from random init. Cost of the failure mode: it looks like a working model with bad weights, sending users into weight-level debugging instead of a one-line class fix.

### Expected behavior

Hard error (or at minimum a prominent warning) when: the checkpoint's `config.model_type` has a registered conversion mapping, AND the resolved class matches ~0% of checkpoint tensors. "You loaded a `<model_type>` checkpoint via `<class>`; its weights require the `<other class>` conversion mapping" would turn hours of debugging into seconds. Secondary question: is the absence of a text-only `AutoModelForCausalLM` load path for this checkpoint layout an intentional policy or an omission?
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
device_map loading OOMs on conversion-op transients: WeightConverter contiguous() runs on destination GPU, unbudgeted by max_memory packing
### System Info

- `transformers` version: 5.14.1
- Platform: Linux-6.17.0-1007-aws-x86_64-with-glibc2.39
- Python version: 3.12.3
- Huggingface_hub version: 1.24.0
- Safetensors version: 0.8.0
- Accelerate version: 1.14.0
- Accelerate config: not found
- DeepSpeed version: not installed
- PyTorch version (accelerator?): 2.12.0a0+git220ecc2 (CUDA)
- Using distributed or parallel set-up in script?: No (single process; accelerate device_map="auto" across 8 GPUs)
- Using GPU in script?: Yes
- GPU type: NVIDIA B300 SXM6 AC (x8, 268.59 GB each)
Supplementary: transformers 5.14.1; torch 2.12.0a0 cu12.9; 8x NVIDIA B300 (268.59 GB); model: Inkling-975B (bf16, converted checkpoint with WeightConverter ops).

### Who can help?

@CyrilVallez (model loading) @SunMarc (Big Model Inference / device_map)

### Information

- [ ] The official example scripts
- [x] My own modified scripts

### Tasks

- [ ] An officially supported task in the `examples` folder (such as GLUE/SQuAD, ...)
- [x] My own task or dataset (give details below)

### Reproduction

Mechanism: for checkpoints with registered conversion ops (`WeightConverter` + `Interleave`/`Chunk`), the op chain (incl. `.contiguous()`) executes on the tensor's **destination GPU** during load (`core_model_loading.py`, v5.14.x). For a large converted tensor this is a ~2x transient (source view + contiguous output). `max_memory` packing budgets only the resident parameter bytes, so when a GPU is packed near its cap, the **last large converted tensor assigned to it OOMs** even though the final resident model fits.
 
Observed (Inkling 975B, `device_map="auto"`, `max_memory={i:"240GiB"}`): fused-expert tensors (`gate_up_proj`, [256, 6144, 6144] bf16 ≈ 18 GiB; ~36 GiB transient with conversion) OOM reproducibly at the last MoE layer packed onto each GPU — failing layers {18, 27, 36, 45, 54, 63}, i.e. one per device boundary. Trimmed traceback:
```
torch.OutOfMemoryError: CUDA out of memory. Tried to allocate 18.00 GiB (GPU 2; ...)
  File ".../transformers/core_model_loading.py", line 202, in convert
    tensor = op(tensor).contiguous()
```
Workaround that confirms the accounting gap: lowering `max_memory` headroom by ~1x-largest-converted-tensor per GPU loads cleanly (wasting that memory at steady state).

### Expected behavior

`device_map` packing should account for conversion-op transients, e.g.: (a) subtract the largest per-device converted-tensor transient from each device budget during packing; or (b) execute conversion ops on CPU (or the source buffer) above a size threshold and move the converted result; or (c) document that converted checkpoints require ~largest-tensor headroom. Happy to provide full logs or test a patch.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
MPS: DynamicCache produces NaN logits mid-decode in generate() (transformers >=5.2, regression from 5.0)
## Summary

On Apple Silicon (MPS), transformers **>= 5.2.0** produces NaN logits during autoregressive `generate()` with the default cache (DynamicCache), surfacing as:

```
RuntimeError: probability tensor contains either `inf`, `nan` or element < 0
  File ".../transformers/generation/utils.py", line 2808, in _sample
    next_tokens = torch.multinomial(probs, num_samples=1).squeeze(1)
```

Setting **`cache_implementation="static"` avoids it entirely**. transformers **5.0.0 is stable** on the identical workload and identical torch; 5.2.0, 5.8.1 and 5.14.1 all reproduce — so the regression entered with the 5.2 cache refactor and is still present.

## Key diagnostic facts

Instrumenting `torch.multinomial` in the live failure (rather than a synthetic repro) established:

- The failing `generate` is **single-sequence** — `probs.shape == (1, vocab)`, no padding, so this is **not** the fully-masked-row / SDPA-mask issue (pytorch#156707).
- The **entire logits row** is NaN (`nan_count == vocab_size`), and it happens **mid-decode** — after ~900 successful sampling steps in the run, not at the first token.
- It is **intermittent**: single-shot `generate()` probes (even multi-turn, batched, LoRA, gradient-checkpointed, exact GenerationConfig) never reproduce it; it needs the sustained generation of a real training loop.
- **`cache_implementation="static"` completes cleanly** where DynamicCache fails, on the same version/seed/workload — isolating the fault to the dynamic cache path on MPS.

## Environment

- Apple M4 Max, macOS (Metal), 48 GB
- torch 2.9.1 (constant across all experiments)
- transformers 5.2.0 / 5.8.1 / 5.14.1 reproduce; 5.0.0 does not
- Model: Qwen/Qwen3-0.6B, bfloat16, SDPA, PEFT/LoRA adapter
- Workload: TRL 1.8.0 GRPOTrainer tool-calling rollouts (multi-turn generation)

## Reproduction

Full repro is a TRL GRPO tool-rollout run (open source: nolabs-ai/hedgehog). A minimal standalone repro has been elusive precisely because the fault needs sustained/pipelined decode pressure — single `generate()` calls always succeed. Happy to run diagnostics on the affected hardware.

## Workaround

`cache_implementation="static"` in the generation config. (In isolation this is ~as fast as dynamic; in a loop with varying shapes it recompiles per shape and is ~3x slower without torch.compile — but it is correct.)

## Ask

Either the MPS DynamicCache path needs the same numerical guard the static path has, or triage toward the underlying torch MPS behavior if that's where the corruption originates.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
GitForCausalLM double-shifts the training loss and leaks targets across batch rows (regression from #35875)
### System Info

- `transformers`: main (`7ea2320c76`), also present in every release since v4.49
- Code-level bug, weight-independent — reproducible on CPU, no GPU or pretrained weights needed

### Who can help?

@zucchini-nlp

### Description

`GitForCausalLM.forward` shifts the labels manually and then hands the result to `self.loss_function`, which shifts them a **second** time. The model is trained to predict token `t + 2` from position `t` instead of `t + 1`.

`src/transformers/models/git/modeling_git.py:1081-1092`:

```python
if labels is not None:
    # we are doing next-token prediction; shift prediction scores and input ids by one
    num_image_tokens = self.git.encoder.layer[0].attention.self.image_patch_tokens
    shifted_logits = logits[:, num_image_tokens:-1, :].contiguous()
    labels = labels[:, 1:].contiguous()              # shift #1
    loss = self.loss_function(
        shifted_logits.view(-1, self.config.vocab_size),
        labels.view(-1),                             # binds positionally to `labels`
        vocab_size=self.config.vocab_size,
        **kwargs,
    )
```

`GitForCausalLM` resolves `loss_type` to `"ForCausalLM"`, so `self.loss_function` is `ForCausalLMLoss`. Its signature is `(logits, labels, vocab_size, num_items_in_batch, ignore_index, shift_labels)`, so the already-shifted tensor binds to `labels` and `shift_labels` stays `None`. `src/transformers/loss/loss_utils.py:61-64` then does:

```python
if shift_labels is None:
    labels = nn.functional.pad(labels, (0, 1), value=ignore_index)
    shift_labels = labels[..., 1:].contiguous()      # shift #2
```

Two things follow from this. First, the targets are off by one extra position. Second — and this is the part that does not show up in the loss value alone — the manual shift flattens the labels to 1-D *before* the call, so the internal pad-and-slice operates on the flattened tensor and the shape stays consistent (`N → N+1 → N`). No error is raised, and each batch row's final target is silently pulled in from the **next row** of the batch.

### Regression

This was correct until #35875 ("Fix model kwargs", `28f73bc307`), which mechanically swapped the loss implementation but left the manual shift in place:

```diff
-            loss_fct = CrossEntropyLoss()
-            loss = loss_fct(shifted_logits.view(-1, self.config.vocab_size), labels.view(-1))
+            loss = self.loss_function(
+                shifted_logits.view(-1, self.config.vocab_size),
+                labels.view(-1),
```

`CrossEntropyLoss` does not shift, `ForCausalLMLoss` does. This is the same regression mechanism that was fixed for Moonshine in #46784.

I checked the rest of what #35875 touched. On current main only three call sites still combine a manual shift with `self.loss_function`: `csm` is correct (it passes `labels=None, shift_labels=shift_labels`), `moshi` has the same bug but is already covered by the open #36928, and `git` is the remaining unfixed one.

### Reproduction

CPU, no pretrained weights:

```python
import torch
from torch.nn import CrossEntropyLoss

from transformers import GitConfig, GitForCausalLM
from transformers.models.git.configuration_git import GitVisionConfig

torch.manual_seed(0)
vision_config = GitVisionConfig(
    hidden_size=32, num_hidden_layers=2, num_attention_heads=4,
    intermediate_size=37, image_size=32, patch_size=16,
)
config = GitConfig(
    vision_config=vision_config.to_dict(), vocab_size=99, hidden_size=32,
    num_hidden_layers=2, num_attention_heads=4, intermediate_size=37,
)
model = GitForCausalLM(config).eval()

input_ids = torch.randint(3, config.vocab_size, (2, 7))
pixel_values = torch.randn(2, 3, 32, 32)
labels = input_ids.clone()

with torch.no_grad():
    out = model(input_ids=input_ids, pixel_values=pixel_values, labels=labels)

num_image_tokens = model.git.encoder.layer[0].attention.self.image_patch_tokens
shifted_logits = out.logits[:, num_image_tokens:-1, :]
V = config.vocab_size

aligned = CrossEntropyLoss()(shifted_logits.reshape(-1, V), labels[:, 1:].reshape(-1))

# what the code actually computes: a second shift, applied to the flattened targets
flat = labels[:, 1:].reshape(-1)
leaked = torch.nn.functional.pad(flat, (0, 1), value=-100)[1:]
double_shifted = CrossEntropyLoss()(shifted_logits.reshape(-1, V), leaked)

print("model loss            :", out.loss.item())
print("aligned CE (expected) :", aligned.item())
print("double-shifted CE     :", double_shifted.item())
print("matches aligned       :", torch.allclose(out.loss, aligned))
print("matches double-shift  :", torch.allclose(out.loss, double_shifted))
print("row 0 correct targets :", labels[0, 1:].tolist())
print("row 0 actual targets  :", leaked[:6].tolist())
print("row 1 labels          :", labels[1, 1:].tolist())
```

Output on main:

```
model loss            : 4.584834575653076
aligned CE (expected) : 4.646134853363037
double-shifted CE     : 4.584834575653076
matches aligned       : False
matches double-shift  : True
row 0 correct targets : [28, 71, 8, 58, 61, 15]
row 0 actual targets  : [71, 8, 58, 61, 15, 19]
row 1 labels          : [19, 42, 30, 58, 94, 67]
```

The loss matches the double-shifted computation exactly, and row 0's last target (`19`) is row 1's first label.

### Expected behavior

The target for position `t` should be `labels[t + 1]`, and targets must not cross batch-row boundaries.

### Suggested fix

Unlike Moonshine, GIT cannot simply drop the manual shift: `logits` contains `num_image_tokens` leading image positions that have to be sliced off regardless. Passing `shift_labels` explicitly suppresses the internal shift, which is the convention already used by `csm` (`modeling_csm.py:619-621`):

```diff
             shifted_logits = logits[:, num_image_tokens:-1, :].contiguous()
-            labels = labels[:, 1:].contiguous()
+            shift_labels = labels[:, 1:].contiguous()
             loss = self.loss_function(
-                shifted_logits.view(-1, self.config.vocab_size),
-                labels.view(-1),
+                logits=shifted_logits,
+                labels=None,
                 vocab_size=self.config.vocab_size,
+                shift_labels=shift_labels,
                 **kwargs,
             )
```

Keeping the tensors 2-D also removes the cross-row leak, since `ForCausalLMLoss` flattens them itself. With this applied, the repro above prints `4.646135` for both the model loss and the aligned CE. I have the fix and a regression test ready (the full `tests/models/git` suite passes: 190 passed, 297 skipped) and am happy to open a PR if you agree with the direction.

> Disclosure: this investigation and the proposed patch were prepared with AI assistance, and reviewed and verified by me.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.

[New model] PersonaPlex (full-duplex speech model, based on Moshi)
### Model description

# [Moshi] Modernize for PersonaPlex: modular + processor + WeightConverter + #36928 fix

# What does this PR do?

**Our research team:** @b-re-w, @un1876, @jookite, @capyjin, @haesol-shin

We are using [NVIDIA PersonaPlex](https://huggingface.co/nvidia/personaplex-7b-v1) in an ongoing research project on full-duplex spoken dialogue. In the course of that research — at [latentforge/transformers-moshi](https://github.com/latentforge/transformers-moshi) — Moshi has been modernized to match current transformers conventions, and PersonaPlex support is being built on top of it. Rather than keeping that work on a fork, I would like to contribute it here. The overall work:

1. Converts Moshi to the modular format (`modular_moshi.py`)
2. Adds `MoshiProcessor` and feature extraction
3. Migrates checkpoint conversion to `WeightConverter`, removing `convert_moshi_transformers.py`
4. Fixes the double-shift in loss computation reported in #36928 — a bug we ran into ourselves and resolved the same way, with that report as our reference
5. **Builds toward PersonaPlex support — the reason for 1–4.** This is the model our research runs on: we have been studying the released checkpoint and building the implementation to fit the actual PersonaPlex model. That work is in progress on the fork and will land in a follow-up, but it is what shaped 1–4, so I would rather put it in front of you here than surface it after the fact.

**The code in this PR is items 1–4; item 5 is what they are for.** (1) and (2) apply conventions that `kyutai_speech_to_text` — the model that inherits from Moshi — already follows, so this also lets the downstream model sit on a parent that is no longer the odd one out. (3) follows the v5 dynamic weight loading API. (4) is the bug reported in #36928 — we hit it ourselves in our own training runs, and resolved it the same way with that report as our reference; measurements below.

Related: while looking through open issues, I found that Moshi appears in #39588's list of models still lacking a modular file (`moshi (2512 lines in modeling file)`) — if this contribution lands, it looks like that entry would be resolved along the way.

For (5), see [Next step: PersonaPlex](#next-step-personaplex) below — what I have already found in the checkpoint, the direction I am building toward, and the questions I would like your input on now rather than once the code is written.

## Why: Moshi is the only model in its own family still on the legacy pattern

Moshi is the base of this family — `kyutai_speech_to_text` inherits directly from it:

```python
# src/transformers/models/kyutai_speech_to_text/modular_kyutai_speech_to_text.py
from ..moshi.modeling_moshi import MoshiModel, MoshiPreTrainedModel

class KyutaiSpeechToTextPreTrainedModel(MoshiPreTrainedModel): ...
class KyutaiSpeechToTextModel(MoshiModel): ...
```

Yet the child was added with the current conventions while the base it derives from was never migrated:

| | `kyutai_speech_to_text` | `moshi` (before this PR) |
|---|---|---|
| `modular_*.py` | yes | no |
| `processing_*.py` | yes | no |
| `feature_extraction_*.py` | yes | no |

This shows up directly in user-facing code. Kyutai STT exposes a single processor:

```python
processor = KyutaiSpeechToTextProcessor.from_pretrained(model_id)
inputs = processor(ds[0]["audio"]["array"])
```

while Moshi requires assembling the feature extractor and the tokenizer by hand — this is the current docs example:

```python
feature_extractor = AutoFeatureExtractor.from_pretrained("kyutai/moshiko-pytorch-bf16")
tokenizer = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained("kyutai/moshiko-pytorch-bf16")
user_input_values = feature_extractor(raw_audio=audio_sample, sampling_rate=feature_extractor.sampling_rate, return_tensors="pt")
```

Moshi is a text + audio model and the processor convention has a first-class `audio` argument, so a `MoshiProcessor` seemed like the natural fit. `KyutaiSpeechToTextProcessor` is the closest reference in the family, so I followed its shape rather than inventing a new one.

## The four changes in this PR

### 1. Modular conversion

Pure refactor, no behavior change. Verified with `check_modular_conversion.py` and the existing test suites (below).

### 2. MoshiProcessor and feature extraction

Wraps the feature extractor and the tokenizer into a single processor, following `KyutaiSpeechToTextProcessor`. This is the only part of the PR that adds new public API.

### 3. Checkpoint conversion via WeightConverter

Registers Moshi in `conversion_mapping.py` so the original checkpoint loads directly through `from_pretrained`. Since the conversion then happens at load time, `convert_moshi_transformers.py` is no longer needed and is removed in this PR.

Two things I would like your call on here:

- This one touches `conversion_mapping.py`, which is a central file rather than something contained in the model folder. If you would rather keep the standalone script and skip this part, I am happy to drop it — it is a separate commit.
- I scoped this to Moshi only. `kyutai_speech_to_text` still has its own `convert_*.py` script, so the two are inconsistent on this axis after this PR.

### 4. Double-shift in loss computation (fixes #36928)

This is the bug reported in #36928 — we ran into it ourselves in our own training runs, and resolved it the same way, with that report as our reference. `MoshiForCausalLM.forward` states its own intent in a comment, then does something else:

```python
# Shift so that tokens < n predict n      <- the stated goal
shift_logits = logits[..., :-1, :].contiguous()
shift_labels = labels[..., 1:].contiguous()
...
loss = self.loss_function(shift_logits, shift_labels, ...)   # positional
```

Because the class name contains `ForCausalLM`, `LOSS_MAPPING` resolves `self.loss_function` to `ForCausalLMLoss`, which carries the *same* comment and shifts again when its `shift_labels` argument is `None`. The two positional arguments land on `logits`/`labels`, so the `shift_labels` switch never engages and the shift happens twice.

**The experiment asks one question:** does the loss the model reports score `logits[t]` against `labels[t+1]` — what the comment promises — or against `labels[t+2]`?

**Data and model.** A tiny randomly initialized Moshi and one fixed input. Random data is enough because the alignment is a property of the code, not of the data:

```python
torch.manual_seed(42)   # fixes the weights
model = MoshiForCausalLM(MoshiConfig(vocab_size=99, hidden_size=32, num_hidden_layers=2,
                                     num_attention_heads=2, num_key_value_heads=2, ffn_dim=64)).eval()
torch.manual_seed(7)    # fixes the input
input_ids = torch.randint(0, 99, (1, 8));  labels = input_ids.clone()
```

**Procedure.** The same script runs twice; the only thing that changes in between is `modeling_moshi.py` (`git checkout`). Each run records the loss the model reports, plus two candidate answers computed from the same logits with plain `F.cross_entropy` — no transformers loss code, so the code under test never grades itself:

```python
with torch.no_grad():
    out = model(input_ids=input_ids, labels=labels)             # what the model reports
ref_1 = F.cross_entropy(logits[0, :-1], labels[0, 1:]).item()   # scored against labels[t+1]
ref_2 = F.cross_entropy(logits[0, :-2], labels[0, 2:]).item()   # scored against labels[t+2]
```

**Result** — raw output of the two runs:

```
before: {"loss": 4.550253, "match_ref1": false, "match_ref2": true,  "logits_sum": 2.3901}
after:  {"loss": 4.551546, "match_ref1": true,  "match_ref2": false, "logits_sum": 2.3901}
```

The identical `logits_sum` confirms both runs saw the same weights and input, so the flip can only come from the file: the reported loss reproduces one candidate to six decimals — before the fix it *is* the 2-shift value, after it *is* the 1-shift value. (The two candidates sit close together only because an untrained model scores ≈ `ln(99) ≈ 4.6` either way; the evidence is the exact match, not the gap. `LlamaForCausalLM` and `GPT2LMHeadModel` under the same harness both match `ref_1`.)

**Severity, on data whose answer is known by construction.** Build logits so that position `t` is certain about `labels[t+1]`, with a 60-logit gap between the right token and every other one. Any correctly aligned loss must read ≈ 0 here — no reference formula needed:

```python
logits = torch.full((1, 6, 20), -30.0)
for t in range(5):
    logits[0, t, labels[0, t + 1]] = 30.0
```

| logits built so that… | before | after |
|---|---|---|
| position `t` predicts `labels[t+1]` | **60.0** | **0.0** |
| position `t` predicts `labels[t+2]` | **0.0** | **60.0** |

Chance level here is `ln(20) ≈ 3.0`; 60.0 is the price of being maximally confident and wrong. The pre-fix code scores 0.0 for predicting two tokens ahead and 60.0 for predicting the next one — the opposite of what its own comment asks for.

<details>
<summary>Self-contained reproduction script (~25 lines)</summary>

```python
# pip install torch, then run once per file state:
#   python repro_shift.py                                        # with the fix
#   git checkout src/transformers/models/moshi/modeling_moshi.py
#   python repro_shift.py                                        # without it
import json

import torch
import torch.nn.functional as F

from transformers import MoshiConfig
from transformers.models.moshi.modeling_moshi import MoshiForCausalLM

torch.manual_seed(42)   # fixes the weights
model = MoshiForCausalLM(MoshiConfig(vocab_size=99, hidden_size=32, num_hidden_layers=2,
                                     num_attention_heads=2, num_key_value_heads=2, ffn_dim=64)).eval()
torch.manual_seed(7)    # fixes the input
input_ids = torch.randint(0, 99, (1, 8))
labels = input_ids.clone()

with torch.no_grad():
    out = model(input_ids=input_ids, labels=labels)
logits = out.logits.float()
loss = out.loss.item()
ref_1 = F.cross_entropy(logits[0, :-1], labels[0, 1:]).item()   # scored against labels[t+1]
ref_2 = F.cross_entropy(logits[0, :-2], labels[0, 2:]).item()   # scored against labels[t+2]
print(json.dumps({"loss": round(loss, 6),
                  "match_ref1": abs(loss - ref_1) < 1e-5,
                  "match_ref2": abs(loss - ref_2) < 1e-5,
                  "logits_sum": round(logits.sum().item(), 4)}))
```

</details>

**The fix** removes the manual shift (which duplicates what `ForCausalLMLoss` already does, including the `.float()` upcast, the flatten and the `.to(device)`) and passes the tensors by keyword, matching `modeling_llama.py`:

```python
loss = self.loss_function(logits=logits, labels=labels, vocab_size=self.config.vocab_size, **kwargs)
```

This is a separate commit and it does change behavior, so it is easy to drop if you would rather land it via #36928 itself. Note the keyword form also makes the original mistake structurally impossible. If you would like the alignment locked in, I am happy to add the `ref_1` identity as a regression test in this PR.

## These changes also affect kyutai_speech_to_text

Because `kyutai_speech_to_text` imports from `moshi.modeling_moshi`, converting Moshi to modular is not a Moshi-only change. I ran the Kyutai suite as part of this PR, and there are no regressions:

| Check | Result |
|---|---|
| `ruff` (moshi + kyutai) | clean |
| modular consistency (moshi + kyutai) | exit 0 |
| `check_copies` | exit 0 |
| Moshi tests | 200 passed |
| Kyutai tests | 105 passed |

`kyutai_speech_to_text` is the only model in the library that inherits from Moshi, so it is the full blast radius of changes 1–3. Change 4 is scoped to `MoshiForCausalLM.forward`, which Kyutai does not inherit (it subclasses `MoshiModel` / `MoshiPreTrainedModel`), so its loss path is untouched.

## Would you like this split into separate PRs?

The commits are separated by concern:

- modular conversion — pure refactor, no behavior change
- processor / feature extraction — new public API
- weight conversion — `WeightConverter` + removal of the convert script
- loss fix — behavior change, fixes #36928

I kept them together because they are one "bring Moshi up to current conventions" pass, but I am happy to split them — in particular the last two are self-contained and can be dropped or landed separately.

## Next step: PersonaPlex

This is item (5) from the top — the model our research is built on, and the reason changes 1–4 exist. Support is already in development on the fork; the code will come in a follow-up, but I would like the approach settled here, in this thread. Fitting it to the released checkpoint is how I ran into the `dep_q` difference below.

**About the model.** Per its model card, PersonaPlex finetunes Moshi (Moshiko weights) and adds a "Hybrid System Prompt" mechanism that combines text-based role conditioning with audio-based voice prompting.

- Paper: [arXiv:2602.06053](https://arxiv.org/abs/2602.06053)
- Weights: [nvidia/personaplex-7b-v1](https://huggingface.co/nvidia/personaplex-7b-v1)
- Original code: [github.com/NVIDIA/personaplex](https://github.com/NVIDIA/personaplex)

**What I have verified so far.** The released PersonaPlex checkpoint trains its depth transformer with `dep_q=16` — it predicts both the agent and the user audio streams — whereas the released Moshi checkpoint uses `dep_q=8` (agent stream only). So there is at least a config-level difference beyond the prompt-handling logic.

**The direction I am currently building toward.** The `kyutai_speech_to_text` pattern: its own model folder with a `modular_personaplex.py` inheriting from Moshi, plus a `WeightConverter` so the original NVIDIA checkpoint loads directly.

## Questions

1. **Splitting the PRs** — if we proceed, should the Moshi modernization and the PersonaPlex support go as separate PRs?

2. **The #36928 loss fix** — is it OK to fold that fix into this PR?
   - That PR currently has merge conflicts and has been inactive for a while.
   - If the fix lands here, could #36928 then be closed as resolved — with credit to its author?

3. **PersonaPlex shape** — a lighter path also seems possible: since PersonaPlex is ultimately a finetune of Moshi, it might work without a new model class — loading the checkpoint into the existing Moshi classes, with `dep_q=16` as a config value and the system-prompt handling in the processor. Which of the two would fit the library better?

This modernization came out of our research rather than being an end in itself. It would be great to see it land upstream instead of staying on a fork — and if it does, we hope it makes a useful contribution to the library. I am happy to take it wherever you want it to go: split it, drop any part of it, or rework things to match a convention I have missed.

Every change was reviewed and tested by the authors — the reproduction script and the loss measurements above were run and verified by us, and the test results (Moshi 200, Kyutai 105) were produced locally.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
Question about overriding bnb_4bit_compute_dtype for pre-quantized checkpoints
### System information

- `transformers`: 5.13.1
- `bitsandbytes`: 0.49.2
- `accelerate`: 1.14.0
- `huggingface_hub`: 1.23.0
- `safetensors`: 0.8.0
- PyTorch: 2.11.0+cu128
- CUDA: 12.8
- Python: 3.12.13
- Platform: Google Colab / Linux
- GPU: NVIDIA Tesla T4
- CUDA capability: 7.5
- Native BF16 support: false
- Distributed or parallel setup: no
- Model: `unsloth/gemma-2-9b-it-bnb-4bit`
- Model revision: `27b027bcbb6b1861b02551d5c699d5d07f29610a`

### Description

Hi, I noticed a small behavior when loading a pre-quantized bitsandbytes checkpoint.

This may be expected behavior, but I could not find a supported way to override the saved 4-bit compute dtype at load time, so I thought it might be worth documenting.

The checkpoint stores:

```json
"bnb_4bit_compute_dtype": "bfloat16"
```

I passed an explicit `BitsAndBytesConfig` with:

```python
bnb_4bit_compute_dtype=torch.float16
```

Transformers emitted a warning indicating that the checkpoint's existing `quantization_config` would be used.

After loading:

- `model.config.quantization_config` still contained `bfloat16`;
- all 294 `bitsandbytes.nn.Linear4bit` modules used `torch.bfloat16`;
- the explicitly requested FP16 compute dtype was not applied.

### Minimal reproduction

```python
import warnings

import bitsandbytes as bnb
import torch
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, BitsAndBytesConfig

model_id = "unsloth/gemma-2-9b-it-bnb-4bit"
revision = "27b027bcbb6b1861b02551d5c699d5d07f29610a"

requested_config = BitsAndBytesConfig(
    load_in_4bit=True,
    bnb_4bit_quant_type="nf4",
    bnb_4bit_use_double_quant=True,
    bnb_4bit_compute_dtype=torch.float16,
)

with warnings.catch_warnings(record=True) as caught:
    warnings.simplefilter("always")

    model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(
        model_id,
        revision=revision,
        quantization_config=requested_config,
        device_map={"": 0},
        dtype=torch.float16,
        trust_remote_code=False,
    )

linear4bit_modules = [
    module
    for module in model.modules()
    if isinstance(module, bnb.nn.Linear4bit)
]

print("Requested compute dtype:")
print(requested_config.bnb_4bit_compute_dtype)

print("\nLoaded quantization config:")
print(model.config.quantization_config)

print("\nLinear4bit module count:")
print(len(linear4bit_modules))

print("\nLoaded Linear4bit compute dtypes:")
print({module.compute_dtype for module in linear4bit_modules})

print("\nWarnings:")
for warning in caught:
    print(f"{warning.category.__name__}: {warning.message}")
```

Observed:

```text
Requested compute dtype:
torch.float16

Linear4bit module count:
294

Loaded Linear4bit compute dtypes:
{torch.bfloat16}
```

The loaded quantization configuration also retained:

```text
bnb_4bit_compute_dtype = bfloat16
```

### Manual workaround

Changing the modules after loading worked:

```python
for module in model.modules():
    if isinstance(module, bnb.nn.Linear4bit):
        module.compute_dtype = torch.float16
        module.compute_type_is_set = True
```

After this change, all 294 modules reported `torch.float16`.

### Small performance observation

This was only a small diagnostic, not a general benchmark.

On the Tesla T4, two repeated short deterministic generations produced identical output with both compute dtypes:

| Compute dtype | Mean generation speed |
|---|---:|
| BF16 | approximately 6.87 tokens/s |
| FP16 | approximately 7.37 tokens/s |

FP16 was approximately 7% faster in this small test.

The T4 does not have native BF16 support in this environment. The default `torch.cuda.is_bf16_supported()` check returned `True`, while the native-only check returned `False`.

### Expected behavior / question

I understand that preserving the saved quantization configuration for an already quantized checkpoint may be intentional.

Is there currently a supported way to override only `bnb_4bit_compute_dtype` while retaining the saved 4-bit weights and the other quantization settings?

If the current behavior is intended, one of the following small improvements might still be useful:

- document that a passed compute dtype does not override the saved value for pre-quantized checkpoints;
- include the conflicting saved and requested compute dtypes in the warning;
- allow `bnb_4bit_compute_dtype` as a safe runtime loading override;
- optionally warn when BF16 compute is selected on a GPU without native BF16 support.

This did not cause incorrect output in my small test, and the manual workaround works, so I consider this a low-priority usability issue rather than a critical bug.

Issue #25901 appears related to loading attributes for an already quantized configuration, but it concerns GPTQ and does not appear to cover this specific bitsandbytes compute-dtype case.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.

Two systematic bugs in examples/pytorch/*_no_trainer.py: broken --resume_from_checkpoint auto-discover branch, and wrong eval loss/perplexity on partial batches
### System Info

- `transformers`: `main` (as of 2026-07-16)
- Affected: **every `*_no_trainer.py` example** under `examples/pytorch/`
- No dependency-specific reproducer needed — these are pure Python control‑flow / accounting bugs.

I hit two independent, systematic bugs in the Accelerate‑based `no_trainer` examples. Both are copy‑pasted across ~15 example scripts, so filing one issue covering both. Happy to send a single PR that fixes them all.

## Bug 1 — `--resume_from_checkpoint` (no argument) is broken: "load most recent checkpoint" branch is dead code

### Where

Every `*_no_trainer.py` example, e.g.:

- [`examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_clm_no_trainer.py#L595-L610`](https://github.com/huggingface/transformers/blob/main/examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_clm_no_trainer.py#L595-L610)
- `run_mlm_no_trainer.py`, `run_fim_no_trainer.py`, `run_qa_no_trainer.py`, `run_qa_beam_search_no_trainer.py`, `run_translation_no_trainer.py`, `run_summarization_no_trainer.py`, `run_glue_no_trainer.py`, `run_ner_no_trainer.py`, `run_swag_no_trainer.py`, `run_image_classification_no_trainer.py`, `run_semantic_segmentation_no_trainer.py`, `run_instance_segmentation_no_trainer.py`, `run_object_detection_no_trainer.py`, `run_mim_no_trainer.py`

15 files, same code:

```python
if args.resume_from_checkpoint:
    if args.resume_from_checkpoint is not None or args.resume_from_checkpoint != "":
        checkpoint_path = args.resume_from_checkpoint
        path = os.path.basename(args.resume_from_checkpoint)
    else:
        # Get the most recent checkpoint
        dirs = [f.name for f in os.scandir(os.getcwd()) if f.is_dir()]
        dirs.sort(key=os.path.getctime)
        path = dirs[-1]
        checkpoint_path = path
        path = os.path.basename(checkpoint_path)
```

### Problem

The inner condition `args.resume_from_checkpoint is not None **or** args.resume_from_checkpoint != ""` is **always true**:

- If `args.resume_from_checkpoint is None` → left side is `False`, right side `None != ""` is `True` → overall `True`.
- If `args.resume_from_checkpoint == ""` → left side `True` → overall `True`.
- Any other string → overall `True`.

So the `else` branch (the "get the most recent checkpoint" path) is **dead code**. There is no code path in the example that can pick up the newest checkpoint automatically. It should be `and`, not `or` — this was almost certainly a typo when the branch was introduced.

Additionally, `if args.resume_from_checkpoint:` above already excludes both `None` and `""`, so passing `--resume_from_checkpoint ""` doesn't reach the `else` either. The intended UX (pass the flag with no value → auto‑discover latest) currently doesn't work anywhere.

### Repro

```bash
# Assume ./output/epoch_0/ was saved by a previous run.
python examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_clm_no_trainer.py \
    --model_name_or_path sshleifer/tiny-gpt2 \
    --dataset_name wikitext --dataset_config_name wikitext-2-raw-v1 \
    --output_dir ./output \
    --resume_from_checkpoint ""     # or omit the value from a shell wrapper
```

The `if args.resume_from_checkpoint:` guard treats `""` as falsy and the block is skipped entirely — the "auto‑discover" flow can never fire.

### Suggested fix

```python
if args.resume_from_checkpoint is not None and args.resume_from_checkpoint != "":
    checkpoint_path = args.resume_from_checkpoint
    path = os.path.basename(args.resume_from_checkpoint)
else:
    # Get the most recent checkpoint
    dirs = [f.name for f in os.scandir(os.getcwd()) if f.is_dir()]
    dirs.sort(key=os.path.getctime)
    path = dirs[-1]
    checkpoint_path = path
    path = os.path.basename(checkpoint_path)
```

…and probably rework the outer `if args.resume_from_checkpoint:` to also accept a sentinel (e.g. `"latest"`) so the auto‑discover path is actually reachable. Two options — happy to defer to maintainer preference.

---

## Bug 2 — Perplexity / eval loss is silently wrong on the last (partial) eval batch

### Where

At least three files (identical line):

- [`examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_clm_no_trainer.py#L668`](https://github.com/huggingface/transformers/blob/main/examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_clm_no_trainer.py#L668)
- [`examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_mlm_no_trainer.py#L698`](https://github.com/huggingface/transformers/blob/main/examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_mlm_no_trainer.py#L698)
- [`examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_fim_no_trainer.py#L858`](https://github.com/huggingface/transformers/blob/main/examples/pytorch/language-modeling/run_fim_no_trainer.py#L858)

```python
losses.append(accelerator.gather_for_metrics(loss.repeat(args.per_device_eval_batch_size)))
```

### Problem

`loss.repeat(args.per_device_eval_batch_size)` uses the **configured** eval batch size, not the size of the actual batch. On the last eval batch this is almost always wrong:

- With `drop_last=False` (the default here) the last batch is a **partial** batch. The tensor of "losses" for that batch is padded to `per_device_eval_batch_size` copies of the same scalar loss instead of being sized to the real number of examples.
- Then `gather_for_metrics` sees a fixed size on every rank and cannot correctly drop the trailing padding, so those repeated copies of the last mean loss get **over‑counted** in the final `torch.mean(losses)` and `math.exp(eval_loss)`.

Net effect: reported **perplexity and eval loss are biased** whenever the eval dataset size is not divisible by `world_size × per_device_eval_batch_size`. The bias is small on huge eval sets and dominant on small ones (a common case for unit tests and CI).
---

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
examples/training/distributed_training.py crashes on import: LOCAL_RANK/WORLD_SIZE/RANK are overwritten by OMPI_* vars
### System Info

- `transformers`: main (as of 2026-07-16)
- File: [`examples/training/distributed_training.py`](https://github.com/huggingface/transformers/blob/main/examples/training/distributed_training.py)

### Who can help?

@ArthurZucker @muellerzr — this looks like leftover WIP from the distributed training example.

### Reproduction

Run the example with the launcher the top comment says it supports (`torch.distributed.launch` / `torchrun`), i.e. **without** OpenMPI:

```bash
torchrun --nproc_per_node=2 --nnodes=1 examples/training/distributed_training.py --backend nccl
```

This immediately crashes with:

```
KeyError: 'OMPI_COMM_WORLD_LOCAL_RANK'
```

### Expected behavior

The script should run under either launcher (`torchrun`/`torch.distributed.launch` **or** `mpirun`), since the docstring at the bottom shows both.

### Root cause

At the top of the file the same three variables are assigned twice, back‑to‑back, from two different launcher conventions:

```python
# Environment variables set by torch.distributed.launch
LOCAL_RANK = int(os.environ["LOCAL_RANK"])
WORLD_SIZE = int(os.environ["WORLD_SIZE"])
WORLD_RANK = int(os.environ["RANK"])

LOCAL_RANK = int(os.environ["OMPI_COMM_WORLD_LOCAL_RANK"])
WORLD_SIZE = int(os.environ["OMPI_COMM_WORLD_SIZE"])
WORLD_RANK = int(os.environ["OMPI_COMM_WORLD_RANK"])
```

Effects:

1. The `LOCAL_RANK` / `WORLD_SIZE` / `RANK` block is dead code — it's immediately overwritten.
2. When launched with anything other than OpenMPI, the module raises `KeyError` on import, before `argparse` even runs.
3. When launched with `mpirun`, the first block still raises `KeyError` because `LOCAL_RANK`/`WORLD_SIZE`/`RANK` aren't set.

So as shipped, the example only works if **both** launcher conventions set their env vars at the same time, which is essentially never.

### Suggested fix

Pick the launcher based on which env vars are actually present, e.g.:

```python
if "OMPI_COMM_WORLD_LOCAL_RANK" in os.environ:
    LOCAL_RANK = int(os.environ["OMPI_COMM_WORLD_LOCAL_RANK"])
    WORLD_SIZE = int(os.environ["OMPI_COMM_WORLD_SIZE"])
    WORLD_RANK = int(os.environ["OMPI_COMM_WORLD_RANK"])
else:
    # torchrun / torch.distributed.launch
    LOCAL_RANK = int(os.environ["LOCAL_RANK"])
    WORLD_SIZE = int(os.environ["WORLD_SIZE"])
    WORLD_RANK = int(os.environ["RANK"])
```

Happy to send a PR if the maintainers agree with this direction.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
GlmMoeDsaConfig: legacy `num_experts` unconditionally overrides explicit `n_routed_experts` (sibling of #46739)
### System info

- `transformers` `main` (verified against `src/transformers/models/glm_moe_dsa/configuration_glm_moe_dsa.py` today)
- Python 3.12, torch 2.11, vLLM 0.25.1
- Affected checkpoint: [`0xSero/GLM-5.2-504B-Nvidia`](https://huggingface.co/0xSero/GLM-5.2-504B-Nvidia) —
  `GlmMoeDsaForCausalLM`, **no `auto_map`**, so this is the in-library config class, not remote code.

### Who can help?

This is a sibling of #46739 (`head_dim` → `qk_rope_head_dim`), which was resolved by #46338 by dropping the alias
and setting the value explicitly in `__post_init__`. The same clobber pattern still exists for `num_experts`.

### Description

`GlmMoeDsaConfig.__post_init__` contains an **unconditional** backward-compat re-route:

```python
# configuration_glm_moe_dsa.py (main), lines 161-163
# BC: re-route `num_experts` to `n_routed_experts`
if (num_experts := kwargs.get("num_experts")) is not None:
    self.n_routed_experts = num_experts
```

If a `config.json` contains **both** keys, the **legacy `num_experts` overwrites the modern, explicit
`n_routed_experts`** — the deprecated key wins. I'd expect a BC shim to be a *fallback* (apply only when
`n_routed_experts` was not explicitly provided), not an override.

This is exactly the shape of #46739, which you fixed in #46338 for `head_dim`.

### Reproduction

```python
from transformers import AutoConfig
M = "0xSero/GLM-5.2-504B-Nvidia"   # config.json has n_routed_experts: 168 AND num_experts: 256

AutoConfig.from_pretrained(M)                        # -> n_routed_experts = 256   ← JSON says 168!
AutoConfig.from_pretrained(M, num_experts=168)       # -> n_routed_experts = 256   ← kwarg cannot help
AutoConfig.from_pretrained(M, n_routed_experts=168)  # -> n_routed_experts = 168
# after deleting num_experts from config.json:       # -> n_routed_experts = 168   ← correct
```

The `num_experts=168` kwarg cannot fix it because the clobber runs during `__post_init__`, before
`from_pretrained` applies kwargs as attributes.

**Expected:** `n_routed_experts` = 168 (the explicit value, and the one matching the checkpoint's tensors).
**Actual:** 256, silently.

### Why it matters in practice

This is not hypothetical. Pruned/distilled GLM-5.2 derivatives in the wild ship **both** keys, because the pruning
tool updates `n_routed_experts` while the stale `num_experts` is inherited from the base config. The resulting
config reports an expert count contradicting **both its own JSON and its own tensors** (verified via
`model.safetensors.index.json`: exactly 168 contiguous routed experts, indices 0..167).

Downstream, vLLM builds `FusedMoE` for 256 experts that do not exist → 64 experts/rank instead of 42 →
**~111 GB/GPU instead of ~80 GB/GPU** → `torch.OutOfMemoryError` on a 94.97 GiB card
(`vllm/model_executor/layers/quantization/modelopt.py:1458`, `create_weights`). vLLM's log shows
`Local/global number of experts: 64/256` where `42/168` is correct. vLLM itself is innocent — it reads
`config.n_routed_experts` correctly and is simply handed a wrong config.

Deleting the stale key makes the model load at 79.1 GB/GPU and serve correctly. Verified on 4× RTX PRO 6000
Blackwell (sm_120).

### Suggested fix

Make the BC re-route a fallback rather than an override, e.g.:

```python
# BC: fall back to legacy `num_experts` only when `n_routed_experts` was not explicitly provided
if "n_routed_experts" not in kwargs and (num_experts := kwargs.get("num_experts")) is not None:
    self.n_routed_experts = num_experts
```

(Or follow the #46338 precedent more directly.) A warning when both keys are present and disagree would also have
saved a lot of debugging here — the current failure is a confusing OOM several layers downstream, with nothing
pointing at the config.

Happy to open a PR if useful.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
## Flaky test: `IndexError` — bbox coordinate values out of 0-1000 range
### System Info

### Affected tests

Multiple model tests that use random bounding box generation fail with:

```
IndexError: The `bbox` coordinate values should be within 0-1000 range.
```

This affects `layoutlm`, `layoutlmv2`, `layoutlmv3`, `lilt`, `pp_doclayout_v2` — any model whose `modeling_*.py` validates bbox coordinates against a hard 0-1000 range.

### Root cause

The bbox coordinates are randomly generated in tests but not clamped to [0, 1000]. When random values exceed the range, the validation in the model's forward pass raises `IndexError`. This is a test-input-generation bug, not a model bug.

### Relevant code

- `src/transformers/models/layoutlm/modeling_layoutlm.py:102` — raises the error
- `src/transformers/models/layoutlmv2/modeling_layoutlmv2.py:81`
- `src/transformers/models/layoutlmv3/modeling_layoutlmv3.py:121`
- `src/transformers/models/lilt/modeling_lilt.py:157`
- `src/transformers/models/pp_doclayout_v2/modeling_pp_doclayout_v2.py:488`

### Proposed fix

Clamp randomly generated bbox values to [0, 1000] in the test input preparation, or change the model validation to clamp instead of raising an error (matching `pp_doclayout_v2`'s own `clamp_(0.0, 1000.0)` behavior).


### Who can help?

_No response_

MetalConfig quantization: batched generate silently corrupts all rows after the first — affine_qmm_t computes only batch element 0 of 3D inputs (verified, one-line fix)
### System Info

```
- `transformers` version: 5.13.1
- Platform: macOS-26.5.2-arm64-arm-64bit
- Python version: 3.11.15
- Huggingface_hub version: 1.23.0
- Safetensors version: 0.8.0
- Accelerate version: 1.14.0
- Accelerate config: not found
- DeepSpeed version: not installed
- PyTorch version (accelerator?): 2.13.0 (MPS)
- kernels version: 0.15.2
- Device: Apple M4 Max, 36 GB, MPS backend
- Using distributed or parallel set-up in script?: No
```

### Who can help?

@MekkCyber @vasqu

### Information

- [ ] The official example scripts
- [x] My own modified scripts

### Tasks

- [ ] An officially supported task in the `examples` folder
- [x] My own task or dataset (give details below)

### Reproduction

Models quantized with `MetalConfig` (bits=4 and bits=8 identical) generate correctly at
batch size 1, but at batch size > 1 only the first row is correct; every later row's
argmax collapses to token 0 (decoding as `!!!!...`). Deterministic — repeated runs are
bit-identical.

**Model-level repro** (greedy, same prompt duplicated — every row should match batch 1):

```python
import torch
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM, AutoTokenizer, MetalConfig

MODEL = "Qwen/Qwen3-0.6B"
tok = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(MODEL)

def generate(model, batch):
    ids = tok(["The capital of France is"] * batch, return_tensors="pt").to("mps")
    with torch.inference_mode():
        out = model.generate(**ids, max_new_tokens=20, do_sample=False)
    return [tok.decode(o[ids["input_ids"].shape[1]:], skip_special_tokens=True) for o in out]

q = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(
    MODEL, quantization_config=MetalConfig(bits=8), dtype=torch.bfloat16
).eval().to("mps")
print(generate(q, 2))
# ['" Paris. The capital of Italy is Rome. ..."', '"!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!"']
# row 0 == batch-1 output exactly; row 1 garbage. Unquantized bf16: all rows correct.
```

**Root cause (verified at kernel level, no model involved).** `MetalLinear.forward`
passes its input to `affine_qmm_t` as-is; during HF decode that input is 3D
`[batch, 1, hidden]`. Calling the kernel directly with a random quantized weight and
checking each output row against `x @ dequant(W).T`:

| input shape | result |
|---|---|
| `[B, K]` 2D, any B | all rows correct |
| `[1, S, K]` any S | all rows correct |
| `[B, 1, K]`, B > 1 | **batch element 0 correct, elements 1+ garbage** |
| `[2, 4, K]` | **rows 0–3 (batch elem 0) correct, rows 4–7 (elem 1) garbage** |

Identical pattern for bits=4/8 × bf16/fp16. The `[2, 4, K]` case pins it: the kernel
computes the **entire first batch element** and never touches the rest — it treats the
input as 2D `[shape[-2], K]`, ignoring the leading batch dimension. The garbage rows are
bit-identical across repeated calls. Probe script:

```python
import torch
from transformers.integrations.metal_quantization import (
    _affine_quantize_tensor, _affine_dequantize_tensor, _get_metal_kernel)

kernel = _get_metal_kernel()
torch.manual_seed(0)
K, N, GROUP, BITS = 2048, 1024, 64, 4
wp, sc, bi = _affine_quantize_tensor(torch.randn(N, K), GROUP, BITS)
w_deq = _affine_dequantize_tensor(wp, sc, bi, GROUP, BITS).to("mps")
wp, sc, bi = wp.to("mps"), sc.to("mps").bfloat16(), bi.to("mps").bfloat16()

for shape in [(2, K), (2, 1, K), (2, 4, K)]:
    x = torch.randn(*shape, device="mps", dtype=torch.bfloat16)
    y = kernel.affine_qmm_t(x, wp, sc, bi, GROUP, BITS)
    ref = (x.reshape(-1, K).float() @ w_deq.t()).reshape(*shape[:-1], N)
    err = ((y.float() - ref).abs().amax(-1) / ref.abs().amax(-1)).flatten()
    print(shape, [f"{e:.3f}" for e in err.tolist()])
# (2, 2048)       ['0.005', '0.006']            <- 2D fine
# (2, 1, 2048)    ['0.006', '9.874']            <- 3D: only batch elem 0 computed
# (2, 4, 2048)    ['0.005', ..., '9.9e+30', ...] <- rows 0-3 fine, 4-7 garbage
```

**Fix (verified).** Flattening 3D inputs to 2D around the kernel call makes batched
generate fully correct — with this patch all batch-4 rows match the batch-1 output
exactly:

```python
def forward(self, input):                      # MetalLinear.forward
    if input.dim() == 3:
        b, s, k = input.shape
        return _orig_forward(self, input.reshape(b * s, k)).reshape(b, s, -1)
    return _orig_forward(self, input)
```

Either `MetalLinear.forward` should flatten to 2D before calling `affine_qmm_t`
(one line, no kernel change needed — happy to open a PR), or the kernel should handle
the batch dimension of 3D inputs.

**Possibly relevant:** the kernel repo ships builds for torch 2.8 / 2.9 / 2.10 only
(`build/torch{28,29,210}-metal-aarch64-darwin`); under torch 2.13 the `kernels` loader
selects the `torch210` build. Reproduced on that combination.

**Impact:** any batched `generate()` with a Metal-quantized model on MPS silently
corrupts all sequences after the first — no error, no warning. Found while benchmarking
nvidia/canary-qwen-2.5b (speech LLM): int4 batch-32 transcription WER went from 2.1%
(batch 1) to 98% (batch 32). Batch 1 is unaffected.

### Expected behavior

Every row of a batched `generate()` should produce the same output as batch size 1 for
the same (duplicated, greedy-decoded) prompt — as batch element 0 already does, as the
2D-flatten patch produces, and as the unquantized bf16 model does for all rows.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
f2py: replace eval() in .f2py_f2cmap parsing with a restricted parser
### Summary

`numpy/f2py/capi_maps.py` (`load_f2cmap_file`) parses the f2cmap file with
`eval(f.read().lower(), {}, {})`. Because Python re-injects `__builtins__`
into an empty globals dict, this evaluates arbitrary Python from the file —
e.g. `__import__('os').system(...)`. The `.f2py_f2cmap` file is also
auto-loaded from the current working directory.

I understand f2py treats its working directory as trusted (like a Makefile
or setup.py), so this is a hardening/defense-in-depth improvement, not a
reported vulnerability.

### Compatibility note (important)

A naive switch to `ast.literal_eval` would break existing usage: the
documented format and both test fixtures use the `dict(...)` constructor
form, e.g.
`dict(real=dict(real64='double'), integer=dict(int64='long long'))`
(see doc/source/f2py/advanced/use_cases.rst and
numpy/f2py/tests/src/f2cmap/.f2py_f2cmap). `ast.literal_eval` rejects
`dict(...)` calls.

### Proposed fix

A small restricted AST evaluator that accepts exactly the two documented
forms — dict literals `{...}` and `dict(...)` keyword calls — plus scalar
constants, and raises `ValueError` on anything else. This preserves 100%
of legitimate usage while removing the code-execution path.

I'd like to submit a PR for this.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
DOC: numpy.ma.vander docstring documents unsupported `increasing` parameter
### Issue with current documentation:

`numpy.ma.vander` reuses the `numpy.vander` docstring via `ma.doc_note`, but its implementation accepts fewer arguments than the inherited documentation describes.

https://github.com/numpy/numpy/blob/848a57d5b97fc3c17e7ff4f5be83d09991f52b22/numpy/ma/extras.py#L2243-L2255

Since the wrapper reuses the upstream docstring, the published documentation for `numpy.ma.vander` (https://numpy.org/doc/stable/reference/generated/numpy.ma.vander.html, and likewise on the current devdocs) describes the API as:

```text
vander(x, N=None, increasing=False)
```

including the `increasing` parameter and an example using:

```python
>>> np.vander(x, increasing=True)
```

However, the callable API of `numpy.ma.vander` is:

```python
>>> import inspect
>>> import numpy as np
>>> inspect.signature(np.ma.vander)
<Signature (x, n=None)>
```

Attempting to use the documented keyword argument raises a `TypeError`:

```python
>>> import numpy as np

>>> x = np.ma.array([1, 2, 3, 5])
>>> np.ma.vander(x, increasing=True)
Traceback (most recent call last):
...
TypeError: vander() got an unexpected keyword argument 'increasing'
```

As a result, the published documentation does not match the current implementation.

### Idea or request for content:

I’d like some guidance on the intended behavior before I open a PR, as there seem to be two reasonable options. 

1. Add support for the `increasing` parameter and forward it to `numpy.vander`, so the implementation matches the interface described in the inherited documentation.
2. Replace the inherited docstring with one specific to the wrapper, documenting only the arguments that `numpy.ma.vander` actually supports. 

I’m happy to work on whichever approach best fits the intended design of `numpy.ma.vander`.
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
ENH: Improve the ergonomics of StringDType <-> fixed-width string casting
### Proposed new feature or change:

Casting StringDType to a fixed-width string currently requires an explicit size:

```python
>>> np.array(["hello", "world!"], dtype="T").astype("S")
TypeError: Casting from StringDType to a fixed-width dtype with an unspecified size is not currently supported, specify an explicit size for the output dtype instead.

The above exception was the direct cause of the following exception:

TypeError: cannot cast dtype StringDType() to <class 'numpy.dtypes.BytesDType'>.
```

Object arrays already support this: 

```python
>>> np.array(["hello"], dtype=object).astype("S")
array([b'hello'], dtype='|S5')
```

I propose StringDType do the same, via a new branch in `find_descriptor_from_array` next to the existing object branch. Since that function backs `astype`, `np.array`/`np.asarray`, `PyArray_CastToType`, and nditer `op_dtypes`, all conversion entry points update together.

I also propose changing the cast safety of the sized fixed-width to StringDType casts to safe, since they cannot silently lose data. The StringDType to fixed-width direction would keep same-kind cast safety, with its current truncating behavior. For reference, currently we do:

```python
>>> np.array(["hello"], dtype="S").astype("T", casting="safe")
TypeError: Cannot cast array data from dtype('S5') to StringDType() according to the rule 'safe'
```

```python
>>> np.array(["hello"], dtype="T").astype("S8")
array([b'hello'], dtype='|S8')

>>> np.array(["hello"], dtype="T").astype("S8", casting='safe')
TypeError: Cannot cast array data from StringDType() to dtype('S8') according to the rule 'safe'
```

### Why make these changes?

The current workaround, `arr.astype(f"S{np.strings.str_len(arr).max()}")`, cannot be computed at all for arrays containing nulls with a non-string `na_object`, even though the sized casts themselves succeed on such arrays by converting nulls to the NA's string repr:

```python
>>> arr = np.array(["abc", np.nan], dtype=np.dtypes.StringDType(na_object=np.nan))
>>> np.strings.str_len(arr)
ValueError: The length of a null string is undefined
>>> arr.astype("U3")
array(['abc', 'nan'], dtype='<U3')
```

Casting a fixed-width string to StringDType can never lose data, yet code that gates conversions on `casting="safe"` rejects it:

```python
>>> np.can_cast("U8", "T")
False
```

Making this cast safe fits NumPy's existing definition of cast safety: no *silent* data loss, with loud runtime errors allowed. For example, the fixed-width `S` to `U` cast is safe, yet it raises on non-ASCII bytes rather than mangling them, and `S` to StringDType behaves the same way:

```python
>>> np.can_cast("S1", "U1")
True
>>> np.array([b"\xff"], dtype="S1").astype("U1")
UnicodeDecodeError: 'ascii' codec can't decode byte 0xff in position 0: ordinal not in range(128)
```

The other direction keeps same-kind cast safety.
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.

### How does this issue affect you or how did you find it:

Transient CI failure.

* #24512 is a previous issue highlighting that there are known thread safety issues with eigenvalue
* OpenMathLib/OpenBLAS#5836 resolved an issue with thread locking; the fix for that issue will be included in OpenBLAS 0.3.34, but Android tests currently use 0.3.33. It's unclear (to me, at least) if this fix will also address the eigenvalue convergence issue.
* #31649 introduced an explicit test xfail for GEMM tests related to the OpenBLAS version. 


Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
BUG: np.piecewise uses collections.abc.Callable isinstance check, which mypy flags as an error
### Describe the issue:

In _function_base_impl.py, piecewise checks whether each item in funclist is callable like this:

`if not isinstance(func, collections.abc.Callable):`

mypy has a known issue with this exact pattern (see python/mypy#6864), where it raises a type-checking error on isinstance checks against collections.abc.Callable. The commonly recommended fix from that thread
is to just use callable(func) instead, which does the same check without confusing static type checkers. It's also the more standard/idiomatic way to check this in Python generally.

Not sure if NumPy's own mypy setup actually runs against this file so this might already be a non-issue but figured it's worth flagging given how small and low-risk the fix is if it does apply

Happy to send a PR swapping it to callable(func) if that's welcome

### Reproduce the code example:

```python
from collections.abc import Callable

def f(x):
    return x

isinstance(f, Callable)
```

### Error message:

```shell
error: Argument 2 to "isinstance" has incompatible type "_SpecialForm";
expected "Union[type, Tuple[Union[type, Tuple[Any, ...]], ...]]"
```

### Python and NumPy Versions:

2.6.0.dev0+git20260715.2fceeef
3.14.0 (v3.14.0:ebf955df7a8, Oct  7 2025, 08:20:14) [Clang 16.0.0 (clang-1600.0.26.6)]
