* gh-154206
<!-- /gh-linked-prs -->

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
test_importlib.test_windows: vendored `get_platform()` misdetects clang-cl builds as `win32`, failing `test_tagged_suffix`
### Bug description:

`test_tagged_suffix` in `Lib/test/test_importlib/test_windows.py` fails on Windows CPython built with clang-cl (`build.bat "/p:PlatformToolset=ClangCL"`, documented in PCbuild/readme.txt; see the reproduction note below about `VSCMD_ARG_TGT_ARCH`). The root cause is the same `sys.version`-truncation misdetection that gh-145410 fixed for `sysconfig.get_platform()` in March 2026 (by moving the check into the `_sysconfig.get_platform()` C accelerator, GH-146145) — but this test computes its expected suffix with a vendored "[Port of distutils.util.get_platform()](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/Lib/test/test_importlib/test_windows.py#L20-L37)" that still carries the pre-fix logic: it sniffs `sys.version.lower()` for `'amd64'`, misses on the truncated clang banner, and falls through to `return sys.platform` → `'win32'`.

```
$ python -m unittest -v test.test_importlib.test_windows -k tagged
test_tagged_suffix (test.test_importlib.test_windows.Frozen_WindowsExtensionSuffixTests.test_tagged_suffix) ... FAIL
test_tagged_suffix (test.test_importlib.test_windows.Source_WindowsExtensionSuffixTests.test_tagged_suffix) ... FAIL

======================================================================
FAIL: test_tagged_suffix (test.test_importlib.test_windows.Frozen_WindowsExtensionSuffixTests.test_tagged_suffix)
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Traceback (most recent call last):
  File "D:\Python\3.16t\Lib\test\test_importlib\test_windows.py", line 154, in test_tagged_suffix
    self.assertIn(expected_tag, suffixes)
    ~~~~~~~~~~~~~^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^
AssertionError: '.cp316t-win32.pyd' not found in ['.cp316t-win_amd64.pyd', '.pyd']
```

(the `Source_` variant fails identically)

**Reproduction note:** the vendored function checks `VSCMD_ARG_TGT_ARCH` first, so the failure only manifests *outside* a VS developer prompt (or with a non-matching target arch); inside `vcvars64` the env var masks it and the test passes. Run the repro from a plain shell.

The interpreter itself is right — the test's expectation is wrong:

```pycon
>>> import sys, sysconfig
>>> sys.version
'3.16.0a0 free-threading build (heads/ft-opt-dirty:2f032556f42, Jul 16 2026, 11:20:12) [Clang 22.1.8 (https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project ca7933e47d3a3451d81e72ac174d'
>>> sysconfig.get_platform()   # fixed by gh-145410
'win-amd64'
>>> from test.test_importlib.test_windows import get_platform; get_platform()   # vendored copy, pre-fix logic
'win32'
>>> import importlib.machinery; importlib.machinery.EXTENSION_SUFFIXES
['.cp316t-win_amd64.pyd', '.pyd']
```

`EXTENSION_SUFFIXES` is built from `PYD_PLATFORM_TAG` in `PC/pyconfig.h` and is correct; only the test's vendored helper is stale.

**Why the banner sniff misses on clang-cl builds:** [`PC/pyconfig.h#L161`](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/PC/pyconfig.h#L161) does put `"] 64 bit (AMD64) with MSC v.NNNN CRT]"` into the clang compiler banner — but [`Python/getversion.c#L18-L20`](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/Python/getversion.c#L18-L20) caps the compiler segment of `sys.version` at `%.80s`, and official LLVM Windows binaries have an 86-char `__clang_version__` (version + URL + full 40-char commit hash — verified against the `llvmorg-22.1.8` tag commit `ca7933e4…`). With the 7-char `"[Clang "` prefix the 80-char cut always lands inside the hash, so the tail carrying `(AMD64)` is truncated away — note the banner above ends 28 characters into the commit hash, inside a never-closed parenthesis, with no `(AMD64)` and no closing bracket. An MSVC banner (`[MSC v.19NN 64 bit (AMD64)]`, ~27 chars) is never truncated, which is why this is clang-specific.

**Prior art:** the same assertion tripped on an early free-threaded Windows buildbot (gh-110359, 2023: `'_d.cp313-win32.pyd' not found in ['_d.cp313t-win_amd64.pyd', '_d.pyd']`). That report's `win32` came from the builder's VS target-arch environment rather than from banner truncation — an MSVC compiler segment is far too short to truncate — but it is the same expected-tag computation going wrong. Only the abi-flag half was addressed there (gh-109740; GH-110422 for gh-110119); the vendored platform sniff was left untouched, and it is what now bites clang-cl builds. Free-threading isn't part of the mechanism either — only the `abi_flags` term of the expected tag depends on it, so a non-FT clang-cl build should fail identically with `.cp316-win32.pyd` vs `.cp316-win_amd64.pyd` (I've only run free-threaded builds myself).

**Suggested fix** (deferring to the maintainers): replace the [`get_platform()` call at L146](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/Lib/test/test_importlib/test_windows.py#L146) with `sysconfig.get_platform()` and delete the vendored function (that call is its only consumer). This does not make the test circular: `SYSCONFIG_PLATFORM` in `Modules/_sysconfig.c` and `PYD_PLATFORM_TAG` in `PC/pyconfig.h` are independent definitions in separate files, so the test still cross-checks two separate code paths. I'm happy to submit a PR — the change is small and test-only.

**Environment / build:** built from `2f032556f42` = local branch `ft-opt` merged with CPython main @ f62050d6574 (2026-07-16), per PCbuild with `build.bat -p x64 --disable-gil --pgo --tail-call-interp "/p:PlatformToolset=ClangCL"`, LLVM 22.1.8 official Windows release, Windows 11 x64; also reproduced on an earlier (June 2026) clang-cl build. All cited code verified unchanged on main as of 2026-07-19; permalinks sha-pinned to 16d0c89b875. My branch carries only build-system tuning (PCbuild props/vcxproj plus a zlib-ng header) and build-regenerated files (hence the `-dirty` banner); `Lib/test/test_importlib/test_windows.py`, `Python/getversion.c`, and `PC/pyconfig.h` are unmodified from upstream.

clang-cl is `PY_SUPPORT_TIER 0`, but PCbuild documents the toolset and it is actively kept working (gh-77532; e.g. gh-146210 in 2026, gh-131278/gh-130090/gh-131035 in 2025) — and the failing logic is a test bug, not a platform gap.

The same 80-char banner truncation also breaks `ctypes.util.find_msvcrt()`'s `"MSC v."` sniff, causing a `test_ctypes.test_errno` failure; filed separately as gh-154199.

### CPython versions tested on:

CPython main branch

### Operating systems tested on:

Windows
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
`ctypes.util.find_msvcrt()` returns "msvcrt.dll" on clang-cl Windows builds, breaking `ctypes.get_errno()`
### Bug description:

On a Windows CPython built with clang-cl (`build.bat "/p:PlatformToolset=ClangCL"`, documented in PCbuild/readme.txt; gh-77532), `ctypes.util.find_msvcrt()` returns `'msvcrt.dll'` instead of `None`. The cause is `sys.version` truncation: `Python/getversion.c` caps the compiler segment at 80 chars (`%.80s`), which cuts off the `"MSC v."` marker that `ctypes.util._get_build_version()` sniffs for, so it falls back to "assume MSVC 6". The practical impact: `CDLL(find_library("c"), use_errno=True)` loads the OS-private legacy `msvcrt.dll`, whose `errno` is a different variable from the ucrt `errno` that `_ctypes` saves/restores around foreign calls — `ctypes.get_errno()` returns stale values (typically `0`) with no exception raised.

Observable symptom: `test.test_ctypes.test_errno.Test.test_open` **fails** on clang-cl builds, while on MSVC builds `find_msvcrt()` returns `None` and the same test silently **skips** (`skipTest("Unable to find C library")`), which is why this has gone unnoticed.

```python
import sys, errno
from ctypes import CDLL, c_char_p, c_int, get_errno
from ctypes.util import find_library, find_msvcrt

print(sys.version)
print(find_msvcrt())          # 'msvcrt.dll'  — expected None, as on MSVC builds
libc = CDLL(find_library("c"), use_errno=True)
libc._open.argtypes = c_char_p, c_int
print(libc._open(b"", 0))     # -1 (call fails, as intended)
print(get_errno())            # 0  — expected errno.ENOENT == 2
```

Observed on a clang-cl build of main:

```
3.16.0a0 free-threading build (heads/ft-opt-dirty:2f032556f42, Jul 16 2026, 11:20:12) [Clang 22.1.8 (https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project ca7933e47d3a3451d81e72ac174d
msvcrt.dll
-1
0
```

```
$ python -m unittest -v test.test_ctypes.test_errno
...
FAIL: test_open (test.test_ctypes.test_errno.Test.test_open)
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Traceback (most recent call last):
  File "...\Lib\test\test_ctypes\test_errno.py", line 25, in test_open
    self.assertEqual(get_errno(), errno.ENOENT)
    ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^
AssertionError: 0 != 2
```

The same build additionally shows both CRTs loaded after the call (`ctypes.util.dllist()` lists `ucrtbase.dll` *and* `msvcrt.dll`), which is the divergence in one line.

**Root cause chain** (permalinks sha-pinned to main @ 16d0c89b875, 2026-07-18; `_get_build_version`/`find_msvcrt`/`find_library` are textually unchanged on today's main, merely shifted a few lines by later unrelated ctypes commits):

1. [`PC/pyconfig.h#L161`](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/PC/pyconfig.h#L161) builds the clang banner as `"[Clang " __clang_version__ "] 64 bit (AMD64) with MSC v." _Py_STRINGIZE(_MSC_VER) " CRT]"` (added in GH-101352) — so the `MSC v.` marker *is intended* to be present.
2. But [`Python/getversion.c#L18-L20`](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/Python/getversion.c#L18-L20) composes `sys.version` with `"%.80s (%.80s) %.80s"` (free-threaded builds use the `"%.80s free-threading build (%.80s) %.80s"` variant — same `%.80s` cap), truncating the compiler segment at 80 chars. Official LLVM Windows binaries have a long `__clang_version__` (`22.1.8 (https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project <40-hex-sha>)` — 86 chars by itself, 93 with the `[Clang ` prefix), so the tail carrying both markers is always truncated away. The full `Py_GetCompiler()` string on my build is 130 chars:
   ```
   [Clang 22.1.8 (https://github.com/llvm/llvm-project ca7933e47d3a3451d81e72ac174dcb5aa28b59d1)] 64 bit (AMD64) with MSC v.1951 CRT]
   ```
   while the `sys.version` compiler segment ends at `...ca7933e47d3a3451d81e72ac174d` — 28 characters into the commit hash, without `MSC v.`, `(AMD64)`, or the closing bracket. (An MSVC banner is ~27 chars and is never truncated, which is why this is clang-specific. The same truncation already broke `sysconfig.get_platform()` on clang-cl builds — gh-145410, fixed in March 2026 by moving the check into C: GH-146145.)
3. [`Lib/ctypes/util.py#L10-L33`](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/Lib/ctypes/util.py#L10-L33): `_get_build_version()` sniffs `sys.version` for `"MSC v."` and, when absent, **returns 6** ("assume the compiler is MSVC 6", a distutils-era assumption).
4. [`Lib/ctypes/util.py#L35-L54`](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/Lib/ctypes/util.py#L35-L54): `find_msvcrt()` maps `version <= 6` to `'msvcrt.dll'`, and [`find_library("c")`](https://github.com/python/cpython/blob/16d0c89b875c520cf5af9da5ba4db133358f742f/Lib/ctypes/util.py#L56-L58) returns that.
5. `msvcrt.dll` maintains its own CRT state; the interpreter and `_ctypes` use the ucrt. The `errno` set by `msvcrt.dll`'s `_open` is never seen by the `use_errno` machinery → `get_errno() == 0`.

Note that the `'msvcrt.dll'` return is reachable *only* through this banner-sniff failure: when the marker survives (e.g. MSVC's `[MSC v.1943 64 bit (AMD64)]`), `_get_build_version()` yields 14.x and `find_msvcrt()` returns `None` — the code comment there cites issue23606, "CRT is no longer directly loadable" (gh-67794/bpo-23606). A clang-cl build links the same ucrt as the MSVC build, so `'msvcrt.dll'` is simply the wrong answer for it. The MSVC-6 fallback would still be meaningful for a toolchain that genuinely links `msvcrt.dll` (classic MinGW), which is worth weighing when choosing between the options below.

**Suggested fix directions** (deferring to the maintainers):

- Minimal: make `_get_build_version()` return `None` instead of `6` when `"MSC v."` is absent, so `find_msvcrt()`/`find_library("c")` behave exactly as on modern MSVC builds and `test_errno` skips consistently. This trades the VC6-era fallback away; if the MinGW case above is considered worth preserving, the next option handles both.
- Alternative: make `find_msvcrt()` report the CRT the interpreter is actually linked against (`ucrtbase.dll` / the `api-ms-win-crt-*` stable ABI) independent of the compiler banner — correct for every toolchain, but it would reverse the bpo-23606 decision that modern MSVC returns `None`.
- Longer-term: stop deriving build facts from `sys.version` string-sniffing altogether; the truncation shows the banner is not a reliable data channel (gh-145410 already moved `sysconfig` off it).

I'm happy to submit a PR for whichever direction a maintainer prefers, with a regression test that exercises `_get_build_version()` against a truncated clang-style banner.

Side observations I can file separately if useful: the `%.80s` cap leaves `sys.version` ending mid-commit-hash without its closing bracket on official-LLVM clang builds, and the clang `_Py_COMPILER` string literal has unbalanced brackets (one `[`, two `]`).

**Environment / build:** CPython main @ f62050d6574 (2026-07-16), built per PCbuild with `build.bat -p x64 --disable-gil --pgo --tail-call-interp "/p:PlatformToolset=ClangCL"`, LLVM 22.1.8 official Windows release, Windows 11 x64. Also reproduced identically on an earlier (June 2026) clang-cl build, and I confirmed the contrasting skip behaviour on an MSVC build of the same source. My working branch carries only build-system tuning (PCbuild props/vcxproj plus a zlib-ng header) and build-regenerated files (hence the `-dirty` banner); the files involved here — `Lib/ctypes/util.py`, `Lib/test/test_ctypes/test_errno.py`, `Python/getversion.c`, `PC/pyconfig.h` — are unmodified from upstream. The failure is not related to free-threading — the mechanism only involves the compiler banner segment.

I'm aware clang-cl is `PY_SUPPORT_TIER 0`; filing since PCbuild documents and actively maintains the toolset (gh-77532, and it is still being kept working — e.g. gh-146210 in 2026, gh-131278/gh-130090/gh-131035 in 2025), the defect is in a stdlib banner-sniff rather than the toolchain, and the same latent defect affects any build whose banner lacks the marker.

Related: gh-77532 / GH-101352 (clang banner introduction), gh-67794 (bpo-23606, `find_msvcrt` → `None` for modern MSVC), gh-70914 (user report that `find_msvcrt()` returns `None` on post-VC6 builds; closed as a duplicate of bpo-23606), gh-145916 (soft-deprecation of `ctypes.util.find_library` — its linked PR touches only the docs, so it removes neither this defect nor the test failure), gh-145410 / GH-146145 (same truncation, `sysconfig` side). The same truncated banner also breaks the vendored `get_platform()` in `Lib/test/test_importlib/test_windows.py`; filed separately as gh-154200.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
Specialize `AttributeError` exceptions from lazy import objects
# Feature or enhancement

Consider specializing `AttributeError` exceptions when custom attributes are accessed on lazy import objects, typically meaning that a lazy import is believed to have been reified when it still isn't reified. It's fairly easy to specialize the exception, so if such accesses are realistic, this might make sense.

## Example

```py
lazy import asyncio

globals()["asyncio"].Task
```

This is the current traceback:
```
Traceback (most recent call last):
  File "/Users/bartosz.slawecki/pydev/gh-153785/t.py", line 3, in <module>
    globals()["asyncio"].Task
AttributeError: 'lazy_import' object has no attribute 'Task'
```

**This is the proposal:**
```
Traceback (most recent call last):
  File "/Users/bartosz.slawecki/pydev/gh-153785/t.py", line 3, in <module>
    globals()["asyncio"].Task
AttributeError: cannot access attribute 'Task' on unresolved lazy import 'asyncio'
```

I do not insist on this being implemented, but we can discuss if it is potentially useful or not. 
Working prototype: https://github.com/python/cpython/compare/main...johnslavik:gh-154196

## Additional context

This was reported by @vstinner in https://github.com/python/cpython/pull/153786#pullrequestreview-4728765088.

Opened as a separate issue because the specialization of lazy import `AttributeError` exceptions, to my mind, does not belong to that pull request.

(The mentioned PR was meant for rare paths involving user-space raises of `AttributeError`, either with attribute name only or with no arguments.)


Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
`_remote_debugging`: Degrade gracefully reads instead of failing the whole read completely
# Bug report

### Bug description:

The implicit problem found in https://discuss.python.org/t/tachyon-97-error-rate/107619 and, subsequently, in #151022 and #151036 is that we're raising exceptions and discarding the whole sample, when we could degrade gracefully and keep most of the information.

There are are many limits from which we can recover gracefully, by truncating the data. In particular: funcnames, filenames, locations, but also some temporary reads from the target.

Raising exceptions causes very high error rates, when it doesn't really need to be the case. Also, we really don't know what might be the limits found in the real apps.

### CPython versions tested on:

CPython main branch

### Operating systems tested on:

macOS

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
use-after-free: functools partial
# Bug report

### Bug description:

Similar to https://github.com/python/cpython/issues/144475 although this is a use after free gap. 

```
def test_call_safety_against_reentrant_mutation(self):
        partial = self.partial

        def original(*args, **kwargs):
            return "original"

        def replacement(*args, **kwargs):
            return "replacement"

        g = None

        class EvilKey(str):
            armed = False
            def __hash__(self):
                if EvilKey.armed and g is not None:
                    EvilKey.armed = False
                    # Reset g, freeing the old (uniquely referenced) args
                    # tuple.  New args of a different length avoid recycling
                    # that freed block, so any dangling read hits freed memory.
                    g.__setstate__((replacement, (), {"k": 1}, None))
                    gc.collect()
                return str.__hash__(self)
            def __eq__(self, other):
                return str.__eq__(self, other)

        # Stored positionals (non-trivial pto->args) plus a stored keyword so
        # the keyword-merge path -- which hashes the call keywords -- runs.
        stored = tuple(object() for _ in range(5))
        g = partial(original, *stored, k=0)
        del stored

        ek = EvilKey("zzz")
        kwargs = {ek: 2}          # hashed here while disarmed: no re-entrancy
        EvilKey.armed = True
        # Must not crash (use-after-free in the C partial before the fix).
        g(**kwargs)
        self.assertFalse(EvilKey.armed)  # the re-entrant __setstate__ ran
```

Inside of `partial_vectorcall` we store a raw pointer of `pto->args` in `pto_args`, however with the EvilKey we can reset `pto->args` causing a UAF gap. 

Unsure how much of an issue this is though.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
locale.strxfrm() crashes on DragonFly BSD: wcsxfrm() does not support zero size
# Crash report

`locale.strxfrm()` segfaults on DragonFly BSD 6.4 on every call, in any locale including C:

```
./python -c "import locale; locale.strxfrm('a')"
Segmentation fault (core dumped)
```
```
#0  wcsncpy ()    from /lib/libc.so.8
#1  wcsxfrm_l ()  from /lib/libc.so.8
#2  wcsxfrm ()    from /lib/libc.so.8
#3  _locale_strxfrm_impl at Modules/_localemodule.c:459
```

This is a regression from gh-130567 (2a2bc82cef9), which introduced the size query `wcsxfrm(NULL, s, 0)`. DragonFly's `wcsxfrm()` does not support zero size: it dereferences the destination (POSIX allows a null pointer when the size is 0), and its C-locale path does the equivalent of `wcsncpy(dest, src, len-1)`, which for len = 0 copies the whole string. In the test suite the crash killed the test_locale worker and aborted the whole run.

The fix is to query the size with a real one-element buffer, which is well-defined everywhere.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
Test suite hangs forever when run as a background job (SIGINT ignored)
# Bug report

When the test suite is started as a shell background job (e.g. `nohup ./python -m test -j8 &`), POSIX shells set SIGINT to SIG_IGN and Python does not install its default SIGINT handler. Then `_thread.interrupt_main()` is a no-op (`PyErr_SetInterruptEx()` does nothing when the handler is SIG_IGN or SIG_DFL) and `asyncio.Runner` does not install its own SIGINT handler, so tests relying on them in `test_asyncio.test_runners` and `test_threading` wait forever. In test_runners the event loop uses a mocked selector, so it busy-spins at 100% CPU while the Mock call history grows without bound (7 GiB in 20 minutes). There is no default test timeout, so the run never finishes.

Reproducer: `sh -c 'trap "" INT; ./python -m test test.test_asyncio.test_runners'`

Platform-independent (verified on Linux, FreeBSD, NetBSD). Note that GNU coreutils `timeout` masks the problem: it catches SIGINT itself, so a child it execs gets SIG_DFL restored.

Fix: restore the default SIGINT handler in regrtest's `setup_process()` when there is no Python-level handler.

cc @malfet @tinglvv @nWEIdia @peterjc123 @mszhanyi @skyline75489 @nbcsm @iremyux @Blackhex @nkhasbag-nv @pytorch/pytorch-dev-infra @gujinghui @EikanWang @fengyuan14 @guangyey @atalman

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
[symm_mem] NCCLAllocMap interior-pointer lookup is O(n) in live allocations
While reading through the NCCL symmetric memory backend I noticed that `find_allocation_covering` in `NCCLSymmetricMemory.cu` uses `ska::flat_hash_map` as its backing container, but the lookup it needs to do — find the allocation whose `[base, base + size)` range covers an arbitrary interior pointer — is a range lookup, which a hash map is the wrong data structure for. So when the fast path (exact base pointer match) misses, it falls back to a full linear scan:

```cpp
NCCLAllocMap::iterator find_allocation_covering(void* ptr, NCCLAllocMap& allocations) {
  auto alloc_it = allocations.find(ptr);
  if (alloc_it != allocations.end()) {
    return alloc_it;
  }
  // falls through to std::find_if over all live allocations
  return find_allocation_covering_linear(ptr, allocations);
}
```

The in-code TODO already calls this out and suggests the fix:

```cpp
// TODO: this linear std::find_if is O(n) in the number of live allocations.
// Make it O(log n) by switching NCCLAllocMap to an ordered map and using
// upper_bound to find the covering allocation.
```

Switching `NCCLAllocMap` to `std::map` (already used in the sibling `CUDASymmetricMemory.hpp` for the same kind of lookup) and replacing the linear scan with `upper_bound` + a single range check is the right fix. There are only two callers of `find_allocation_covering` — `has_allocation()` and `rendezvous()` — both within `NCCLSymmetricMemoryAllocator` and both holding `mutex_`, so the change is self-contained.

**Relevant code:**
- [`NCCLAllocMap` typedef](https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/46bdd05af0f1ee62bc8e109c3b612206cb37bb3e/torch/csrc/distributed/c10d/symm_mem/NCCLSymmetricMemory.cu#L79) — current `ska::flat_hash_map` definition
- [`find_allocation_covering_linear`](https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/46bdd05af0f1ee62bc8e109c3b612206cb37bb3e/torch/csrc/distributed/c10d/symm_mem/NCCLSymmetricMemory.cu#L98-L107) — the `std::find_if` that does the linear scan
- [`find_allocation_covering` + TODO](https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/46bdd05af0f1ee62bc8e109c3b612206cb37bb3e/torch/csrc/distributed/c10d/symm_mem/NCCLSymmetricMemory.cu#L109-L126) — where the fallback is triggered and the TODO lives
- [`has_allocation`](https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/46bdd05af0f1ee62bc8e109c3b612206cb37bb3e/torch/csrc/distributed/c10d/symm_mem/NCCLSymmetricMemory.cu#L626-L629) — one of the two callers

Happy to send a PR.
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
Nightly binary builds failing: `check_binary_symbols.py` smoke test compiles at C++17, but headers now require C++20
## Summary

Since 2026-07-17 the CI smoke test `.ci/pytorch/smoke_test/check_binary_symbols.py`
fails to compile its probe program, taking down every `manywheel-*-test`
job. Nightly binary builds have been red since the 2026-07-19 nightly.
This is a test-harness/header mismatch, not a defect in the built wheels.

## Error looks like

`manywheel-*-test` (and other binary `*-test`) jobs fail during
`check_binary_symbols.py` with:

```
RuntimeError: Compilation failed: ...
.../torch/include/torch/csrc/api/include/torch/all.h:5:2: error: #error C++20 or later compatible compiler is required to use PyTorch.
```

Traceback ends in:

```
File ".ci/pytorch/smoke_test/check_binary_symbols.py", line 140, in _compile_and_extract_symbols
    raise RuntimeError(f"Compilation failed: {result.stderr}")
```

Affected job families (all wheel variants — CPU, CUDA, XPU; x86_64,
aarch64, Windows): `manywheel-py3_*-cpu-test`, `manywheel-py3_*-cuda*-test`,
`manywheel-py3_*-xpu-test`, and their `-aarch64` counterparts.

## Root cause

`check_stable_only_symbols()` compiles a probe that includes
`torch/all.h` and `ATen/ATen.h`, pinned at `-std=c++17`:

```python
base_compile_flags = [
    "g++",
    "-std=c++17",
    ...
]
```

#178150 ("[12/12] Enforce C++20 minimum in header guards", commit
`bab118ec759`, landed 2026-07-17) changed the header guards in
`torch/csrc/api/include/torch/all.h` and `aten/src/ATen/ATen.h` from
`__cplusplus < 201703L` to `< 202002L`, so those headers now hard-error
under a pre-C++20 compiler. The smoke-test probe was not updated to
match, so it can no longer compile.

Confirmed on the nightly binary builds:

- 2026-07-18 nightly (`generated-linux-binary-manywheel-nightly`): green;
  its build's `all.h` still guarded on C++17.
- 2026-07-19 nightly: red across all `manywheel-*-test` variants with the
  error above; its build's `all.h` guards on C++20.

## Scope / user impact

- Nightly binary (wheel) builds on `main` are red on the binary-test step.
- Any PR whose base includes `bab118ec759` (i.e. anything rebased past
  2026-07-17) inherits these red `manywheel-*-test` jobs. The wheels
  themselves build and install fine — only the smoke test's own compiler
  flag is stale.

## Fix

#190520 bumps only that one probe (`check_stable_only_symbols`'s
`base_compile_flags`) to `-std=c++20`. The other four checks in the file
(stable / header-only / C-shim) intentionally stay at `-std=c++17`: they
exercise the portable ABI surface, which does not include the
C++20-guarded headers and must remain buildable under the older standard.

## Links

- Broke it: #178150
- Fixes it: #190520


cc @malfet @atalman @tinglvv @nWEIdia @pytorch/pytorch-dev-infra
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
[inductor] Missing barrier on same-kernel global buffer read-back (RAW) causes accuracy failure
### 🐛 Describe the bug

### Summary

When an inductor Triton kernel stores a buffer and then reads it back later in the same kernel, no barrier is emitted between the store and the load. The store and the read-back can end up on different warps, so a warp may read the location before another warp's write is visible - a read-after-write race through global memory.

This is the read-after-write counterpart to the write-after-read guard in `store()` (triton issue #1615). That direction is guarded; store-then-read-back is not.

### Repro
pit_b_224 (timm), inductor + AMP fp16 inference on Intel XPU:

      TORCHINDUCTOR_FORCE_DISABLE_CACHES=1 python benchmarks/dynamo/timm_models.py \
        -d xpu --accuracy --amp --inference --backend=inductor \
        --cold-start-latency -n10 --disable-cudagraphs --only pit_b_224

Result: fail_accuracy (RMSE ~0.4 vs tol ~0.001).

The generated kernel stores `out_ptr0` and reads it back in the reduction loop with nothing in between:

      tl.store(out_ptr0 + (r0_2 + 256*x3), tmp26, r0_mask & xmask)
      ...
      tmp34 = tl.load(out_ptr0 + (r0_2 + 256*x3), r0_mask & xmask, ...)

[linalg] Missing 32-bit LAPACK workspace size checks in SVD, Eig, QR, and Lstsq
### Description

While fixing `linalg.eigh` in PR #190006, we identified that several other linear algebra operations implemented via LAPACK on CPU do not have early validation checks to prevent 32-bit workspace integer overflows.

Because all default CPU builds link against a 32-bit integer LAPACK interface, passing a workspace query response `lwork` (which is returned as a float/double) that exceeds `INT32_MAX` (2,147,483,647) will silently overflow when cast to `int` inside `lapack_work_to_int`. This leads to undefined behavior, memory allocation errors, or backend failures with cryptic errors like:
```
RuntimeError: false INTERNAL ASSERT FAILED ...
linalg.svd: Argument 12 has illegal value.
Most certainly there is a bug in the implementation calling the backend library.
```

### Affected Operators & Formulas

1. **`linalg.svd` (`gesdd`)**:
   - Workspaces: `lwork` and `lrwork` (complex).
   - Under real divide-and-conquer `gesdd`, `lwork` requires roughly `3*min(m, n)^2 + max(max(m, n), 4*min(m, n)^2 + 4*min(m, n))` (when computing full `u` and `vt`).
   - For `m = n = 27,000`, the workspace exceeds `INT32_MAX`.

2. **`linalg.eig` (`geev`)**:
   - Non-symmetric eigenvalue decomposition also queries `lwork` and casts it through `lapack_work_to_int`.

3. **`linalg.qr` (`geqrf`)**:
   - Queries optimal workspace `lwork` and converts to `int` via `lapack_work_to_int`.

4. **`linalg.lstsq` (`gelsd`)**:
   - Divide-and-conquer least squares queries `lwork` and has no early overflow checks.

### Proposal
Implement early CPU size and workspace overflow checks in `TORCH_META_FUNC` for each of these functions, matching the check format added for `linalg.eigh` in PR #190006.

cc: @harsharajkumar-273


cc @jgong5 @mingfeima @XiaobingSuper @sanchitintel @ashokei @jingxu10 @aditew01 @malfet @jianyuh @nikitaved @mruberry @walterddr @Lezcano
Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
[SymmetricMemory] NVSHMEM backend: allocate signal pad within the same allocation as the buffer?
### 🚀 The feature, motivation and pitch

### Proposal

Allocate the signal pad as part of the same allocation as the data buffer in
`NVSHMEMSymmetricMemory`, instead of a separate `nvshmem_malloc`. This mirrors
what `CUDASymmetricMemory` appears to do, and matches an existing
`// TODO: use the same allocation for signal pad` in the NVSHMEM backend
(torch/csrc/distributed/c10d/symm_mem/NVSHMEMSymmetricMemory.cu).

### Motivation

Every `nvshmem_malloc` is a collective, symmetric, barrier-synchronized
operation. Allocating the signal pad separately from the buffer therefore means:

- **2 collective allocations per symmetric tensor** instead of 1 — an extra
  cross-rank barrier on the allocation path.
- **2 order-sensitive allocation sites** that must stay consistent across all
  PEs, instead of a single site.

Folding the pad into the buffer allocation removes both, and aligns the NVSHMEM
backend's layout with the CUDA backend — which seems to be the intent of the
existing TODO.

I'm working on a SymmetricMemory-style backend for a non-CUDA accelerator whose
allocator has the same "every malloc is a collective barrier" semantics as
NVSHMEM, and I'd like to follow the direction PyTorch intends here before
committing to a layout.


### Alternatives

**Keep the separate / lazy signal pad allocation (current behavior).**
This avoids making every symmetric tensor carry a signal pad even when it never
participates in a signaling op. In practice the pad is small and configurable,
and symmetric allocations tend to be few and reused, so co-allocating eagerly
looks like a net win — but I may be missing a reason the current code keeps them
separate (e.g. the pad being sized lazily, VMM-backed heap considerations, or
the shared allocation-tracking structures used across backends).

A middle ground would be to make co-allocation and the pad size configurable, so
the eager layout can be turned off for workloads that allocate many tiny
symmetric tensors.


### Additional context

### Code references (please correct my understanding)

- `NVSHMEMSymmetricMemory` — separate `nvshmem_malloc` for the signal pad, plus
  the `// TODO: use the same allocation for signal pad`: <FILE:LINE permalink>
- `CUDASymmetricMemory` — signal pad within the same allocation block as the
  buffer: <FILE:LINE permalink, if found>

### Questions

1. Is the separate allocation intentional, or purely a not-yet-done TODO?
2. Are there known blockers? e.g. the cross-backend `AllocationRef` bookkeeping,
   the rendezvous handle exchange carrying `buffer_size` / `signal_pad_size`
   separately, `data_ptr`/offset handling for the returned tensor, or avoiding
   regressions in the CUDA backend.
3. Would a PR consolidating the NVSHMEM signal pad into the buffer allocation be
   welcome?

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
[MPS] layer_norm forward kernel variance computation causes divergence from CPU reference
### 🐛 Describe the bug

The MPS forward kernel computes variance in one pass as `E[x²] − E[x]²` and then clamps `var < 1e-6` to zero. For a row with nearly identical values, the two quantities become nearly equal (and possibly large), so the small true variance is lost to rounding noise. Clamping it to zero below a certain level is just a band-aid to avoid the unrealistic case of negative variance, with the negative side effect of also setting valid positive but small variances to zero. This collapses reciprocal of standard deviation to `rsqrt(eps)` and makes the normalized outputs diverge between MPS backend and CPU.

Repro for the issue from 
```python
import torch
import torch.nn.functional as F

# Per-element variance ~9.8e-7 just below the kernel's 1e-6 clamp
# with the eps that ViT-family LayerNorms use (1e-12).
x = torch.tensor([[-9.9e-4, -9.9e-4, 9.9e-4, 9.9e-4]])
print(F.layer_norm(x,            (4,), eps=1e-12))   # CPU
print(F.layer_norm(x.to('mps'),  (4,), eps=1e-12))   # MPS

# Output:
# tensor([[-1.0000, -1.0000,  1.0000,  1.0000]])
# tensor([[-990., -990.,  990.,  990.]], device='mps:0')
```

The fix to avoid the cancellation is to compute the subtraction before the square by using the other identity for variance `E[(x−μ)²]`. This requires rewriting the kernel in a two-pass formulation, but also removes the need for the clamping as we can no longer get negative variances due to the cancellation.

Opening a PR with the suggested changes.

### Versions

Current nightly. MacOS27 beta.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
Improve mean time to detect the issue by adding warning logs when users miss to call destroy_process_group
While I was working on some project, I missed to call destroy_process_group and got error message "terminate called without an active exception". I have written a minimal repro script.

```python
import torch
import os
import torch.multiprocessing as mp
import sys
import time

WORLD_SIZE=5
MASTER_PORT=8118
MASTER_ADDR="127.0.0.1"

def dist_body(rank, result_queue):
    try:
        os.environ["MASTER_ADDR"] = MASTER_ADDR
        os.environ["MASTER_PORT"] = str(MASTER_PORT)
        torch.distributed.init_process_group(
            backend="gloo",
            rank=rank,
            world_size=WORLD_SIZE
        )
        pg = torch.distributed.group.WORLD
        rank_pg = torch.distributed.get_rank(pg)

        # Sleep so that we can use gdb to see the backtrace and check where std::terminate was called
        # time.sleep(20) 

        input_tensors = torch.tensor([rank_pg * 100], dtype=torch.float32)
        output_tensors = [torch.empty(1, dtype=torch.float32) for i in range(WORLD_SIZE)]
        pg.allgather(output_tensors, input_tensors)
        status = f"ok, rank_pg={rank_pg}"
        result_queue.put((rank, status))
    except Exception as e:
        print(e) 
        result_queue.put((rank, f"failed : {e}"))
    finally:
        # Remove destroy process group to reproduce the issue
        torch.distributed.destroy_process_group()


def dist_main():
    world_size = WORLD_SIZE

    ctx = mp.get_context("spawn")
    result_queue = ctx.Queue()
    mp.spawn(
        dist_body,
        args=(result_queue,),
        nprocs= world_size, 
        join=True
    )
    results = [result_queue.get() for _ in range(world_size)]
    for rank, status in sorted(results):
        print(rank, status)
        assert status == f"ok, rank_pg={rank}"

if __name__ == "__main__":
    dist_main()
```

I only realized my simple mistake after debugging for very long time after checking the backtrace using gdb.

It turns out that during the destruction of AsyncAllgatherWork, it tried to decref the tensors after the python interpreter was finalized. 

The proper fix should be to destroy the process group, but I think we can at least improve the mean time to detect this issue by adding some warning logs in pytorch. I have already tried using CPP_BACKTRACE and TORCH_SHOW_CPP_STACKTRACES and it didn't work. 

One of the solutions that I have came up with is that we check if the python interpreter is already destroyed or not before decref and add torch warning logs. 

```C++
void ConcretePyInterpreterVTable::decref(PyObject* pyobj, ...) const {
  // If the interpreter is finalizing, a non-main thread cannot safely take
  // the GIL — doing so gets it forcibly killed via pthread_exit, which unwinds
  // through this noexcept frame and calls std::terminate. Leak the ref instead;
  // the process is going away and the memory is about to be reclaimed anyway.
  if (_Py_IsFinalizing()) {
   TORCH_WARN("Python interpreter is already destroyed ........");
    return;
  }
  pybind11::gil_scoped_acquire gil;
  ...
}
```

I would love to open a PR to fix this issue after discussing the all feasible solutions.

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
[MPS] `torch.nextafter` is a no-op for bfloat16
## 🐛 Describe the bug

On MPS, `torch.nextafter` returns its input unchanged for bfloat16. A sweep over {±0, ±1, ±2, ±smallest normal, ±denormal, max, min, ±inf, nan} pairs gives 180/225 bitwise mismatches vs CPU; the same sweep for float32/float16 matches CPU exactly (denormal handling aside, tracked in #125051).

```python
import torch

a = torch.tensor(1.0, dtype=torch.bfloat16)
b = torch.tensor(2.0, dtype=torch.bfloat16)

torch.nextafter(a, b)                      # 1.0078125 (CPU, correct)
torch.nextafter(a.to("mps"), b.to("mps"))  # 1.0 (unchanged — wrong)
```

Likely cause: `nextafter_functor` in `aten/src/ATen/native/mps/kernels/BinaryKernel.metal` calls `::metal::nextafter`, which has no bfloat overload; the arguments promote to `float`, step one fp32 ULP, and the cast back to bfloat rounds the step away. CPU implements exact bf16 stepping in `c10/util/BFloat16-math.h`, and the MPS kernel does register a bfloat variant, so this doesn't look intentional.

Tests miss it because `test_mps.py::test_nextafter` only covers float16/float32 (its `nextafter(x, y) > x` assertion fails for bfloat16), and OpInfo comparisons can't see 1-ULP errors (see #125028). Related: #124985, #187340.

Reproduced on 2.13.0 and nightly 2.14.0.dev20260718 (Apple M1 Pro).

Analyze this software issue and explain the possible cause and solution.
_scaled_mm: scale_result silently ignored on fp8 output path (CUDA, torch 2.10 / nightly / main)
### 🐛 Describe the bug

`torch._scaled_mm(..., out_dtype=torch.float8_e4m3fn, scale_result=s)` no longer applies `scale_result` to the fp8 output: the fp32 accumulator is cast to fp8 at an implicit scale of 1.0 regardless of `s`. The v1 entry point still validates `scale_result` ("must be a float scalar") but never forwards it. In `_scaled_mm_out_cuda` the call to `_scaled_gemm(...)` omits `scale_result`, and `_scaled_gemm` hardwires the result-scale slot of `cublasCommonArgs` to `std::nullopt`, so `CUBLASLT_MATMUL_DESC_D_SCALE_POINTER` is never set. The in-tree doc comment still promises the behavior ("`scale_result`: a scalar tensor with the scale of the output, only utilized if the output is a float8 type"), so a caller that requests fp8 output with an output scale silently gets unscaled fp8, which can saturate/flush and corrupt downstream.

This is a regression: torch 2.9.1+cu128 honors `scale_result` (the pre-refactor path forwarded `args.scale_result_ptr` into `scaled_gemm`); it broke in the `Blas.cpp` -> `ScaledBlas.cpp` refactor between 2.9.1 and 2.10 and is still present on nightly and main. It only affects the fp8-**output** path with a non-trivial output scale; bf16/fp16/fp32 output (where `scale_result` is documented as not applied) is unaffected.

Source references (main):
- https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/main/aten/src/ATen/native/cuda/ScaledBlas.cpp#L518-L519 - `scale_result` validated, never used.
- https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/main/aten/src/ATen/native/cuda/ScaledBlas.cpp#L665 - `_scaled_gemm(...)` called with no `scale_result`.
- https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/main/aten/src/ATen/native/cuda/ScaledBlas.cpp#L388 - result-scale slot hardwired to `std::nullopt`.
- https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/blob/main/aten/src/ATen/cuda/CUDABlas.cpp#L1874-L1876 - `CUBLASLT_MATMUL_DESC_D_SCALE_POINTER` set only when the pointer is non-null.

Minimal self-contained repro:

```python
import torch

E4M3 = torch.float8_e4m3fn
dev = "cuda"
torch.manual_seed(0)
M, K, N = 32, 16, 32

# Integer operands in {-1,0,1}, K=16 -> accumulated sums in [-16,16], all exact
# in e4m3; 0.5*ref lands on the 0.5 grid (also exact). Any nonzero diff is a real
# bug, not fp reordering.
a_int = torch.randint(-1, 2, (M, K), device=dev)
b_int = torch.randint(-1, 2, (K, N), device=dev)
A = a_int.float().to(E4M3)
B = b_int.float().t().contiguous().t().to(E4M3)  # column-major B

one = torch.tensor(1.0, device=dev)
half = torch.tensor(0.5, device=dev)

o1 = torch._scaled_mm(A, B, scale_a=one, scale_b=one, scale_result=one, out_dtype=E4M3)
o2 = torch._scaled_mm(A, B, scale_a=one, scale_b=one, scale_result=half, out_dtype=E4M3)

ref = (A.float().double() @ B.float().double()).cpu()
o1_eq_o2 = bool(torch.equal(o1.view(torch.int8), o2.view(torch.int8)))
err2 = float((o2.float().double().cpu() - 0.5 * ref).abs().max())

print("torch", torch.__version__)
print("o1 == o2 bitwise:", o1_eq_o2, "(expected False; True == bug)")
print("err deq(o2) vs 0.5*ref:", err2, "(expected 0.0; nonzero == scale_result ignored)")
```

Observed vs expected:

```
Expected (scale_result honored): o1 != o2 bitwise, and deq(o2) == 0.5*ref exactly.

torch 2.9.1+cu128       -> o1 == o2 bitwise: False   err deq(o2) vs 0.5*ref: 0.0   (correct)
torch 2.12.0.dev20260408+cu128 -> o1 == o2 bitwise: True    err deq(o2) vs 0.5*ref: 4.5   (BUG)

On nightly/main o1 == o2 and deq(o2) == ref: the requested output scale of 0.5 had
zero effect. The err=0.0 pass on 2.9.1 also validates the multiply-convention
direction of the oracle, ruling out a repro bug.
```

Related issues: #119135 ("`scale_result` not changing result tensor at all", Feb 2024) is CLOSED (fixed 2024-04-23); 2.9.1 still honors `scale_result`, so the current 2.10+/main behavior is a re-regression of that path introduced by the `Blas.cpp` -> `ScaledBlas.cpp` refactor. #154807 ("FP8 scaled mm lowering ignores scale_result argument", open) is the Inductor-lowering manifestation and is plausibly the same root cause surfacing at the compile layer. Original report for reference: https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/119135 ("In `_scaled_mm`, `scale_result` not changing result tensor at all", Feb 2024) reports the same symptom historically. Note that 2.9.1 in this audit does honor `scale_result`, so the current nightly/main behavior is a re-regression of that path rather than the original report; it may or may not be tracked by the same issue.

Affected: torch 2.12.0.dev20260408+cu128 (nightly, confirmed by run), and release/2.10 and main (per source inspection: same `_scaled_gemm` signature drop). Not affected: torch 2.9.1+cu128 (confirmed by run, `scale_result` honored). Regression window: introduced by the `Blas.cpp` -> `ScaledBlas.cpp` refactor between 2.9.1 and 2.10.
